       <tr> 
        <td class="mbox-image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Farsi.svg/40px-Farsi.svg.png" width="40" height="29" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Farsi.svg/60px-Farsi.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Farsi.svg/80px-Farsi.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="323" data-file-height="235"></td> 
        <td class="mbox-text plainlist" style="vertical-align:middle; font-size:95%;">You may need <a href="/wiki/Help:Arabic" title="Help:Arabic">rendering support</a> to display the <a href="/wiki/Persian_alphabet" title="Persian alphabet">Persian text</a> in this article correctly.</td>

     </table> 
     <p><b>Iran</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/aɪ/ long 'i' in 'tide'">aɪ</span><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'r' in 'rye'">r</span><span title="/æ/ short 'a' in 'bad'">æ</span><span title="'n' in 'no'">n</span></span>/</a></span></span> or <span class="nowrap"><span class="noexcerpt"><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e3/En-us-Iran.ogg" title="Listen"><img alt="Listen" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Speakerlink-new.svg/11px-Speakerlink-new.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Speakerlink-new.svg/17px-Speakerlink-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Speakerlink-new.svg/22px-Speakerlink-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="11" data-file-height="11"></a><sup><span class="IPA" style="color:#00e;font:bold 80% sans-serif;padding:0 .1em"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Iran.ogg" title="File:En-us-Iran.ogg">i</a></span></sup></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ɪ/ short 'i' in 'bid'">ɪ</span><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'r' in 'rye'">r</span><span title="/ɑː/ 'a' in 'father'">ɑː</span><span title="'n' in 'no'">n</span></span>/</a></span></span>;<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Persian_language" title="Persian language">Persian</a>: <span lang="fa" dir="rtl">Irān – ایران</span>‎‎ <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Persian" title="Help:IPA for Persian">[ʔiːˈɾɒːn]</a></span><small class="nowrap metadata">&nbsp;(<a href="/wiki/File:IranPronunciationFarsi.ogg" title="File:IranPronunciationFarsi.ogg"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Speaker_Icon.svg/13px-Speaker_Icon.svg.png" width="13" height="13" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Speaker_Icon.svg/20px-Speaker_Icon.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Speaker_Icon.svg/26px-Speaker_Icon.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="500"></a> <a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/54/IranPronunciationFarsi.ogg" class="internal" title="IranPronunciationFarsi.ogg">listen</a>)</small>), also known as <b>Persia</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'p' in 'pie'">p</span><span title="/ɜːr/ 'ir' in 'bird'">ɜːr</span><span title="/ʒ/ 's' in 'pleasure'">ʒ</span><span title="/ə/ 'a' in 'about'">ə</span></span>/</a></span></span> or <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'p' in 'pie'">p</span><span title="/ɜːr/ 'ir' in 'bird'">ɜːr</span><span title="/ʃ/ 'sh' in 'shy'">ʃ</span><span title="/ə/ 'a' in 'about'">ə</span></span>/</a></span></span>),<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Iranicaonline.org_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Iranicaonline.org-14">[14]</a></sup> officially the <b>Islamic Republic of Iran</b> (<span lang="fa">جمهوری اسلامی ایران – Jomhuri ye Eslāmi ye Irān</span> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Persian" title="Help:IPA for Persian">[d͡ʒomhuːˌɾije eslɒːˌmije ʔiːˈɾɒːn]</a></span>), is a <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">sovereign state</a> in <a href="/wiki/Western_Asia" title="Western Asia">Western Asia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-15">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> It is bordered to the northwest by <a href="/wiki/Armenia" title="Armenia">Armenia</a>, the <i>de facto</i> <a href="/wiki/Nagorno-Karabakh_Republic" title="Nagorno-Karabakh Republic">Nagorno-Karabakh Republic</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan" title="Azerbaijan">Azerbaijan</a>; to the north by <a href="/wiki/Kazakhstan" title="Kazakhstan">Kazakhstan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a> across the <a href="/wiki/Caspian_Sea" title="Caspian Sea">Caspian Sea</a>; to the northeast by <a href="/wiki/Turkmenistan" title="Turkmenistan">Turkmenistan</a>; to the east by <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a>; to the south by the <a href="/wiki/Persian_Gulf" title="Persian Gulf">Persian Gulf</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Oman" title="Gulf of Oman">Gulf of Oman</a>; and to the west by <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> and <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a>. Comprising a land area of 1,648,195&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (636,372&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi), it is the second-largest country in the <a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">Middle East</a> and the 18th-largest in the world. With 78.4 million inhabitants, Iran is the world's 17th-most-populous country.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-15">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-britannica1_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica1-18">[18]</a></sup> It is the only country that has both a <a href="/wiki/Caspian_Sea" title="Caspian Sea">Caspian Sea</a> and an <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean" title="Indian Ocean">Indian Ocean</a> coastline. Iran has long been of <a href="/wiki/Geostrategic" title="Geostrategic" class="mw-redirect">geostrategic</a> importance because of its central location in Eurasia and Western Asia, and its proximity to the <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Hormuz" title="Strait of Hormuz">Strait of Hormuz</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Iran is home to one of the world's oldest <a href="/wiki/Civilizations" title="Civilizations" class="mw-redirect">civilizations</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> beginning with the formation of the <a href="/wiki/Proto-Elamite" title="Proto-Elamite">Proto-Elamite</a> and <a href="/wiki/Elam" title="Elam">Elamite</a> kingdoms in 3200–2800 BC. The <a href="/wiki/Iranian_peoples" title="Iranian peoples">Iranian</a> <a href="/wiki/Medes" title="Medes">Medes</a> unified the area into the first of many empires in 625&nbsp;BC, after which it became the dominant cultural and political power in the region.<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclop.C3.A6dia_Britannica_Encyclopedia_Article:_Media_ancient_region.2C_Iran_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclop.C3.A6dia_Britannica_Encyclopedia_Article:_Media_ancient_region.2C_Iran-4">[4]</a></sup> Iran reached the pinnacle of its power during the <a href="/wiki/Achaemenid_Empire" title="Achaemenid Empire">Achaemenid Empire</a> founded by <a href="/wiki/Cyrus_the_Great" title="Cyrus the Great">Cyrus the Great</a> in 550&nbsp;BC, which at its greatest extent comprised major portions of the ancient world, stretching from parts of the <a href="/wiki/Balkans" title="Balkans">Balkans</a> (<a href="/wiki/Thrace" title="Thrace">Thrace</a>-<a href="/wiki/Macedonia_(region)" title="Macedonia (region)">Macedonia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a>-<a href="/wiki/Paeonia_(kingdom)" title="Paeonia (kingdom)">Paeonia</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Europe" title="Eastern Europe">Eastern Europe</a> proper in the west, to the <a href="/wiki/Indus_Valley" title="Indus Valley" class="mw-redirect">Indus Valley</a> in the east, making it the largest empire the world had yet seen.<sup id="cite_ref-book_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-book-22">[22]</a></sup> The empire collapsed in 330 BC following the conquests of <a href="/wiki/Alexander_the_Great" title="Alexander the Great">Alexander the Great</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Parthian_Empire" title="Parthian Empire">Parthian Empire</a> emerged from the ashes and was succeeded by the <a href="/wiki/Sassanid_Dynasty" title="Sassanid Dynasty" class="mw-redirect">Sassanid Dynasty</a> in 224&nbsp;AD, under which Iran again became one of the leading powers in the world, along with the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman</a>-<a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantine Empire</a>, for a period of more than four centuries.<sup id="cite_ref-Norman_A._Stillman_p._22_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Norman_A._Stillman_p._22-23">[23]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Byzantine_Studies_2006.2C_p._29_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Byzantine_Studies_2006.2C_p._29-24">[24]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>In 633 AD, <a href="/wiki/Rashidun_conquest_of_the_Sassanian_Empire" title="Rashidun conquest of the Sassanian Empire" class="mw-redirect">Rashidun Muslims invaded Iran</a> and conquered it by 651 AD, largely replacing the indigenous faiths of <a href="/wiki/Manichaeism" title="Manichaeism">Manichaeism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Zoroastrianism" title="Zoroastrianism">Zoroastrianism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Levy2009_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Levy2009-25">[25]</a></sup> Iran became a major contributor to the <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Golden_Age" title="Islamic Golden Age">Islamic Golden Age</a>, producing many influential scientists, scholars, artists, and thinkers. Establishment of the <a href="/wiki/Safavid_Dynasty" title="Safavid Dynasty" class="mw-redirect">Safavid Dynasty</a> in 1501, which promoted <a href="/wiki/Twelver_Shia" title="Twelver Shia" class="mw-redirect">Twelver Shia</a> Islam as the official religion, marked one of the most important turning points in Iranian and <a href="/wiki/Muslim_history" title="Muslim history" class="mw-redirect">Muslim history</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Andrew_J._Newman_2006_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Andrew_J._Newman_2006-6">[6]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-savoryeiref_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-savoryeiref-26">[26]</a></sup> Starting in 1736 under <a href="/wiki/Nader_Shah" title="Nader Shah">Nader Shah</a>, Iran reached its greatest territorial extent since the Sassanid Empire, briefly possessing what was arguably the most powerful empire at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-books.google.nl_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-books.google.nl-27">[27]</a></sup> During the 19th century, Iran <a href="/wiki/Russo-Persian_Wars" title="Russo-Persian Wars">irrevocably lost swaths</a> of its territories in the <a href="/wiki/Caucasus" title="Caucasus">Caucasus</a> which made part of the concept of Iran for centuries,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFisherAveryHamblyMelville1991329.E2.80.93330_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFisherAveryHamblyMelville1991329.E2.80.93330-28">[28]</a></sup> to neighboring <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Russia" title="Imperial Russia" class="mw-redirect">Imperial Russia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Timothy_C._Dowling_pp._728-730_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Timothy_C._Dowling_pp._728-730-29">[29]</a></sup> Popular unrest culminated in the <a href="/wiki/Persian_Constitutional_Revolution" title="Persian Constitutional Revolution">Persian Constitutional Revolution</a> of 1906, which established a <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">constitutional monarchy</a> and the country's first <a href="/wiki/Majles" title="Majles" class="mw-redirect">Majles</a> (parliament). Following a <a href="/wiki/1953_Iranian_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="1953 Iranian coup d'état">coup d'état instigated by the U.K. and the U.S.</a> in 1953, Iran gradually became close allies <a href="/wiki/Iran-United_States_relations" title="Iran-United States relations" class="mw-redirect">with the United States and the rest of the West</a>, remained <a href="/wiki/Secularism" title="Secularism">secular</a>, but grew increasingly autocratic.<sup id="cite_ref-Anthony_H._Cordesman_p_22_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Anthony_H._Cordesman_p_22-30">[30]</a></sup> Growing dissent against foreign influence and political repression culminated in the <a href="/wiki/1979_Revolution" title="1979 Revolution" class="mw-redirect">1979 Revolution</a>, which led to the establishment of an <a href="/wiki/Islamic_republic" title="Islamic republic">Islamic republic</a> on 1 April 1979.<sup id="cite_ref-britannica1_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica1-18">[18]</a></sup></p> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Tehran" title="Tehran">Tehran</a> is the country's capital and largest city, as well as its leading cultural and economic center. Iran is a major <a href="/wiki/Regional_power" title="Regional power">regional</a> and <a href="/wiki/Middle_power" title="Middle power">middle power</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-parliament_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-parliament-31">[31]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-petro-hunt_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-petro-hunt-32">[32]</a></sup> exerting considerable influence in <a href="/wiki/Energy_superpower#Iran" title="Energy superpower">international energy security</a> and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(PPP)" title="List of countries by GDP (PPP)">world economy</a> through its large reserves of <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuels" title="Fossil fuels" class="mw-redirect">fossil fuels</a>, which include the largest <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas_reserves_in_Iran" title="Natural gas reserves in Iran">natural gas supply</a> in the world and the fourth-largest proven <a href="/wiki/Oil_reserves" title="Oil reserves">oil reserves</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Reuters.com_November_29_2015c_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reuters.com_November_29_2015c-33">[33]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CIA_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-34">[34]</a></sup> Iran's rich cultural legacy is reflected in part by its 19 UNESCO World Heritage Sites, the fourth-largest number in Asia and 12th-largest in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Iran is a founding member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">UN</a>, <a href="/wiki/Economic_Cooperation_Organization" title="Economic Cooperation Organization">ECO</a>, <a href="/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement" title="Non-Aligned Movement">NAM</a>, <a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_Islamic_Cooperation" title="Organisation of Islamic Cooperation">OIC</a>, and <a href="/wiki/OPEC" title="OPEC">OPEC</a>. Its <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Iran" title="Politics of Iran">political system</a> is based on the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_the_Islamic_Republic_of_Iran" title="Constitution of the Islamic Republic of Iran">1979 Constitution</a> which combines elements of a <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_democracy" title="Parliamentary democracy" class="mw-redirect">parliamentary democracy</a> with a <a href="/wiki/Theocracy" title="Theocracy">theocracy</a> governed by <a href="/wiki/Guardianship_of_the_Islamic_Jurists" title="Guardianship of the Islamic Jurists">Islamic jurists</a> under the concept of a <i><a href="/wiki/Supreme_Leader_of_Iran" title="Supreme Leader of Iran">Supreme Leadership</a></i>. A <a href="/wiki/Demography_of_Iran" title="Demography of Iran" class="mw-redirect">multicultural country</a> comprising numerous ethnic and linguistic groups, most inhabitants are officially <a href="/wiki/Shia" title="Shia" class="mw-redirect">Shia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Persian_language" title="Persian language">Persian</a> is the official language.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup></p> 
     <p></p>

        </ul> </li>

     <p></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span></h2> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Name_of_Iran" title="Name of Iran">Name of Iran</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The term <i><a href="/wiki/Iran_(word)" title="Iran (word)">Iran</a></i> derives directly from <a href="/wiki/Middle_Persian" title="Middle Persian">Middle Persian</a> <i>Ērān</i>, first attested in a 3rd-century inscription at <a href="/wiki/Naqsh-e_Rustam" title="Naqsh-e Rustam">Rustam Relief</a>, with the accompanying <a href="/wiki/Parthian_language" title="Parthian language">Parthian</a> inscription using the term <i>Aryān</i>, in reference to <a href="/wiki/Iranian_people" title="Iranian people" class="mw-redirect">Iranians</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-MacKenzie_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MacKenzie-37">[37]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Middle_Iranian_languages" title="Middle Iranian languages" class="mw-redirect">Middle Iranian</a> <i>ērān</i> and <i>aryān</i> are oblique plural forms of <a href="/wiki/Demonym" title="Demonym">gentilic</a> <i>ēr-</i> (Middle Persian) and <i>ary-</i> (Parthian), both deriving from <a href="/wiki/Proto-Iranian_language" title="Proto-Iranian language">Proto-Iranian</a> <i>*arya-</i> (meaning "<a href="/wiki/Aryan" title="Aryan">Aryan</a>," i.e., "of the Iranians"),<sup id="cite_ref-MacKenzie_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MacKenzie-37">[37]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Schmitt_Aryans1_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schmitt_Aryans1-38">[38]</a></sup> argued to descend from <a href="/wiki/Proto-Indo-European_language" title="Proto-Indo-European language">Proto-Indo-European</a> <i><span title="Proto-Indo-European language" class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap">*ar-yo-</span></i>, meaning "skillful assembler."<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Iranian_languages" title="Iranian languages">Iranian languages</a>, the gentilic is attested as a self-identifier included in ancient inscriptions and the literature of <a href="/wiki/Avesta" title="Avesta">Avesta</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Bailey_Arya_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bailey_Arya-40">[40]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[a]</a></sup> and remains also in other Iranian ethnic names such as <i><a href="/wiki/Ossetians" title="Ossetians">Alans</a></i> (<a href="/wiki/Ossetic_language" title="Ossetic language" class="mw-redirect">Ossetic</a>: Ир – <i>Ir</i>) and <i><a href="/wiki/Iron_dialect" title="Iron dialect">Iron</a></i> (<a href="/wiki/Ossetic_language" title="Ossetic language" class="mw-redirect">Ossetic</a>: Ирон – <i>Iron</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-Schmitt_Aryans1_38-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schmitt_Aryans1-38">[38]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Historically, Iran has been referred to as <i>Persia</i> by <a href="/wiki/Western_world" title="Western world">the West</a>, due mainly to the writings of <a href="/wiki/Greeks" title="Greeks">Greek</a> historians who called Iran <i>Persis</i> (<a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a>: <span lang="el">Περσίς</span>),<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[41]</a></sup> meaning "land of the <a href="/wiki/Persian_people" title="Persian people">Persians</a>." As the most extensive interactions the <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greeks" title="Ancient Greeks" class="mw-redirect">Ancient Greeks</a> had with any outsider was with the Persians, the term persisted, even long after the Persian rule in <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a>. However, <a href="/wiki/Persis" title="Persis">Persis</a> (<a href="/wiki/Old_Persian" title="Old Persian">Old Persian</a>: <i>Pārśa</i>; <a href="/wiki/Modern_Persian" title="Modern Persian" class="mw-redirect">Modern Persian</a>: <i>Pārse</i>) was originally referred to a region settled by Persians in the west shore of <a href="/wiki/Lake_Urmia" title="Lake Urmia">Lake Urmia</a>, in the 9th century BC. The settlement was then shifted to the southern end of the <a href="/wiki/Zagros_Mountains" title="Zagros Mountains">Zagros Mountains</a>, and is today defined as <a href="/wiki/Fars_Province" title="Fars Province">Fars Province</a>.</p> 
     <p>In 1935, <a href="/wiki/Reza_Shah" title="Reza Shah">Reza Shah</a> requested the international community to refer to the country by its native name, <i>Iran</i>. As the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Times" title="New York Times" class="mw-redirect">New York Times</a> explained at the time, "At the suggestion of the Persian Legation in <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a>, the Tehran government, on the Persian New Year, <a href="/wiki/Nowruz" title="Nowruz">Nowruz</a>, March 21, 1935, substituted <i>Iran</i> for <i>Persia</i> as the official name of the country." Opposition to the name change led to the reversal of the decision, and Professor <a href="/wiki/Ehsan_Yarshater" title="Ehsan Yarshater">Ehsan Yarshater</a>, editor of <a href="/wiki/Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Iranica" title="Encyclopædia Iranica">Encyclopædia Iranica</a>, propagated a move to use <i>Persia</i> and <i>Iran</i> interchangeably.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[42]</a></sup> Today, both <i>Persia</i> and <i>Iran</i> are used in cultural contexts; although, <i>Iran</i> is the name used officially in political contexts.<sup id="cite_ref-artarena_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-artarena-44">[43]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Historical and cultural usage of the word <i>Iran</i> is not restricted to the modern state proper.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[44]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[45]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[46]</a></sup> <i>Irānzamīn</i> or <i>Irān e Bozorg</i> (<a href="/wiki/Greater_Iran" title="Greater Iran">Greater Iran</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[47]</a></sup> correspond to territories of the Iranian cultural and linguistic zones. In addition to modern Iran, it includes portions of the <a href="/wiki/Caucasus" title="Caucasus">Caucasus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mesopotamia" title="Mesopotamia">Mesopotamia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anatolia" title="Anatolia">Anatolia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">Central Asia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[48]</a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/History_of_Iran" title="History of Iran">History of Iran</a>
     </div> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prehistory">Prehistory</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Cave_painting_in_Doushe_cave,_Lorstan,_Iran,_8th_millennium_BC.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Cave_painting_in_Doushe_cave%2C_Lorstan%2C_Iran%2C_8th_millennium_BC.JPG/220px-Cave_painting_in_Doushe_cave%2C_Lorstan%2C_Iran%2C_8th_millennium_BC.JPG" width="220" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Cave_painting_in_Doushe_cave%2C_Lorstan%2C_Iran%2C_8th_millennium_BC.JPG/330px-Cave_painting_in_Doushe_cave%2C_Lorstan%2C_Iran%2C_8th_millennium_BC.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Cave_painting_in_Doushe_cave%2C_Lorstan%2C_Iran%2C_8th_millennium_BC.JPG/440px-Cave_painting_in_Doushe_cave%2C_Lorstan%2C_Iran%2C_8th_millennium_BC.JPG 2x" data-file-width="486" data-file-height="330"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Cave_painting_in_Doushe_cave,_Lorstan,_Iran,_8th_millennium_BC.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Cave_painting" title="Cave painting">Cave painting</a> in Doushe cave, 
        <a href="/wiki/Lorestan" title="Lorestan" class="mw-redirect">Lorestan</a>, Iran, 
        <a href="/wiki/8th_millennium_BC" title="8th millennium BC">8th millennium BC</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote">
      Further information: 
      <a href="/wiki/Prehistory_of_Iran" title="Prehistory of Iran">Prehistory of Iran</a> and 
      <a href="/wiki/Archaeological_sites_in_Iran" title="Archaeological sites in Iran">Archaeological sites in Iran</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The earliest archaeological artifacts in Iran, like those excavated at the <a href="/wiki/Kashafrud" title="Kashafrud">Kashafrud</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ganj_Par" title="Ganj Par">Ganj Par</a> sites, attest to a human presence in Iran since the <a href="/wiki/Lower_Paleolithic" title="Lower Paleolithic">Lower Paleolithic</a> era, c. 800,000–200,000 BC.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[49]</a></sup> Iran's <a href="/wiki/Neanderthal" title="Neanderthal">Neanderthal</a> artifacts from the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Paleolithic" title="Middle Paleolithic">Middle Paleolithic</a> period, c. 200,000–40,000 BC, have been found mainly in the <a href="/wiki/Zagros" title="Zagros" class="mw-redirect">Zagros</a> region, at sites such as <a href="/wiki/Warwasi" title="Warwasi">Warwasi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yafteh" title="Yafteh">Yafteh Cave</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Museum_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Museum-51">[50]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[51]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (July 2013)">page&nbsp;needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Around <a href="/wiki/10th_millennium_BC" title="10th millennium BC">10th</a> to <a href="/wiki/8th_millennium_BC" title="8th millennium BC">8th</a> millennium BC, early agricultural communities such as <a href="/wiki/Chogha_Golan" title="Chogha Golan">Chogha Golan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chogha_Bonut" title="Chogha Bonut">Chogha Bonut</a> began to flourish in Iran,<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[52]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[53]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[54]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[55]</a></sup> as well as <a href="/wiki/Susa" title="Susa">Susa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chogha_Mish" title="Chogha Mish">Chogha Mish</a> developing in and around the Zagros region.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[56]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (July 2013)">page&nbsp;needed</span></a></i>]</sup><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[57]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-xinhuaciv_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-xinhuaciv-59">[58]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>The emergence of Susa as a city, as determined by <a href="/wiki/Radiocarbon_dating" title="Radiocarbon dating">radiocarbon dating</a>, dates back to early 4,395&nbsp;BC.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[59]</a></sup> There are dozens of prehistoric sites across the Iranian plateau, pointing to the existence of ancient cultures and urban settlements in the <a href="/wiki/4th_millennium_BC" title="4th millennium BC">4th millennium BC</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-xinhuaciv_59-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-xinhuaciv-59">[58]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-iran-daily_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iran-daily-61">[60]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-iranian.ws_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iranian.ws-62">[61]</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/Bronze_Age" title="Bronze Age">Bronze Age</a>, Iran was home to several civilizations including <a href="/wiki/Elam" title="Elam">Elam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jiroft_culture" title="Jiroft culture">Jiroft</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Zayandeh_River_Culture" title="Zayandeh River Culture">Zayande River</a>. Elam, the most prominent of these civilizations, developed in the southwest of Iran, alongside those in <a href="/wiki/Mesopotamia" title="Mesopotamia">Mesopotamia</a>. The emergence of writing in Elam was paralleled to <a href="/wiki/Sumerian_language#Writing_system" title="Sumerian language">Sumer</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Elamite_cuneiform" title="Elamite cuneiform">Elamite cuneiform</a> was developed since the 3rd millennium BC.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[62]</a></sup> The Elamite Kingdom continued its existence until the emergence of the <a href="/wiki/Medes" title="Medes">Median</a> and <a href="/wiki/Achaemenid" title="Achaemenid" class="mw-redirect">Achaemenid</a> empires. Between 3400 BC until about 2000 BC, northwestern Iran was part of the <a href="/wiki/Kura-Araxes_culture" title="Kura-Araxes culture" class="mw-redirect">Kura-Araxes culture</a> that stretched into the neighbouring regions of the <a href="/wiki/Caucasus" title="Caucasus">Caucasus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Anatolia" title="Anatolia">Anatolia</a>. Since the earliest <a href="/wiki/2nd_millennium_BC" title="2nd millennium BC">2nd millennium BC</a>, <a href="/wiki/Assyria" title="Assyria">Assyrians</a> settled in swaths of western Iran, and incorporated the region into their territories.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Classical_antiquity">Classical antiquity</span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles: 
      <a href="/wiki/Medes" title="Medes">Medes</a>, 
      <a href="/wiki/Achaemenid_Empire" title="Achaemenid Empire">Achaemenid Empire</a>, 
      <a href="/wiki/Seleucid_Empire" title="Seleucid Empire">Seleucid Empire</a>, 
      <a href="/wiki/Parthian_Empire" title="Parthian Empire">Parthian Empire</a> and 
      <a href="/wiki/Sasanian_Empire" title="Sasanian Empire">Sasanian Empire</a>
     </div> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote">

     </div>

      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>During the <a href="/wiki/2nd_millennium_BC" title="2nd millennium BC">2nd millennium BC</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Iranian_peoples" title="Ancient Iranian peoples" class="mw-redirect">Proto-Iranian</a> tribes arrived in Iran from the <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_steppes" title="Eurasian steppes" class="mw-redirect">Eurasian steppes</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[63]</a></sup> rivaling the native settlers of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-Panshin_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Panshin-65">[64]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[65]</a></sup> As <a href="/wiki/Iranian_peoples" title="Iranian peoples">these tribes</a> dispersed into the wider area of <a href="/wiki/Greater_Iran" title="Greater Iran">Greater Iran</a> and beyond, the boundaries of modern Iran were dominated by the <a href="/wiki/Persian_people" title="Persian people">Persian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Medes" title="Medes">Median</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Parthia" title="Parthia">Parthian</a> tribes.</p> 
     <p>From the late 10th to late 7th centuries BC, the Iranian peoples, together with the pre-Iranian kingdoms, fell under the domination of the <a href="/wiki/Assyrian_Empire" title="Assyrian Empire" class="mw-redirect">Assyrian Empire</a>, based in northern <a href="/wiki/Mesopotamia" title="Mesopotamia">Mesopotamia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Georges_Roux_-_Ancient_Iraq_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Georges_Roux_-_Ancient_Iraq-67">[66]</a></sup> Under king <a href="/wiki/Cyaxares" title="Cyaxares">Cyaxares</a>, the Medes and Persians entered into an alliance with <a href="/wiki/Nabopolassar" title="Nabopolassar">Nabopolassar</a> of <a href="/wiki/Babylon" title="Babylon">Babylon</a>, as well as the <a href="/wiki/Scythians" title="Scythians">Scythians</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Cimmerians" title="Cimmerians">Cimmerians</a>, and together they attacked the Assyrian Empire. The civil war ravaged the Assyrian Empire between 616&nbsp;BC and 605&nbsp;BC, thus freeing their respective peoples from three centuries of Assyrian rule.<sup id="cite_ref-Georges_Roux_-_Ancient_Iraq_67-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Georges_Roux_-_Ancient_Iraq-67">[66]</a></sup> The unification of the Median tribes under <a href="/wiki/Deioces" title="Deioces">a single ruler</a> in 728&nbsp;BC led to the foundation of the <a href="/wiki/Median_Empire" title="Median Empire" class="mw-redirect">Median Empire</a> which, by 612&nbsp;BC, controlled the whole Iran and the eastern <a href="/wiki/Anatolia" title="Anatolia">Anatolia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[67]</a></sup> This marked the end of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Urartu" title="Kingdom of Urartu" class="mw-redirect">Kingdom of Urartu</a> as well, which was subsequently conquered and dissolved.<sup id="cite_ref-Sagona2006_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sagona2006-69">[68]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[69]</a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:CyrustheGreatTomb_22059.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/CyrustheGreatTomb_22059.jpg/220px-CyrustheGreatTomb_22059.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/CyrustheGreatTomb_22059.jpg/330px-CyrustheGreatTomb_22059.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/CyrustheGreatTomb_22059.jpg/440px-CyrustheGreatTomb_22059.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2736"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:CyrustheGreatTomb_22059.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> Tomb of 
        <a href="/wiki/Cyrus_the_Great" title="Cyrus the Great">Cyrus the Great</a>, founder of the 
        <a href="/wiki/Achaemenid_Empire" title="Achaemenid Empire">Achaemenid Empire</a>, 
        <a href="/wiki/Pasargadae" title="Pasargadae">Pasargadae</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Gate_of_All_Nations,_Persepolis.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Gate_of_All_Nations%2C_Persepolis.jpg/220px-Gate_of_All_Nations%2C_Persepolis.jpg" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Gate_of_All_Nations%2C_Persepolis.jpg/330px-Gate_of_All_Nations%2C_Persepolis.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Gate_of_All_Nations%2C_Persepolis.jpg/440px-Gate_of_All_Nations%2C_Persepolis.jpg 2x" data-file-width="918" data-file-height="600"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Gate_of_All_Nations,_Persepolis.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> Ruins of the 
        <a href="/wiki/Gate_of_All_Nations" title="Gate of All Nations">Gate of All Nations</a>, 
        <a href="/wiki/Persepolis" title="Persepolis">Persepolis</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>In 550&nbsp;BC, <a href="/wiki/Cyrus_the_Great" title="Cyrus the Great">Cyrus the Great</a>, son of <a href="/wiki/Mandane" title="Mandane" class="mw-redirect">Mandane</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cambyses_I" title="Cambyses I">Cambyses I</a>, took over the Median Empire, and founded the <a href="/wiki/Achaemenid_Empire" title="Achaemenid Empire">Achaemenid Empire</a> by unifying other city states. The conquest of Media was a result of what is called the <i><a href="/wiki/Persian_Revolt" title="Persian Revolt">Persian Revolt</a></i>. The <a href="/wiki/Brouhaha" title="Brouhaha">brouhaha</a> was initially triggered by the actions of the Median ruler <a href="/wiki/Astyages" title="Astyages">Astyages</a>, and was quickly spread to other provinces, as they allied with the Persians. Later conquests under Cyrus and his successors expanded the empire to include <a href="/wiki/Lydia" title="Lydia">Lydia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Babylon" title="Babylon">Babylon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Egypt" title="Ancient Egypt">Egypt</a>, parts of the <a href="/wiki/Balkans" title="Balkans">Balkans</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Europe" title="Eastern Europe">Eastern Europe</a> proper, as well as the lands to the west of the <a href="/wiki/Indus_River" title="Indus River">Indus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oxus_River" title="Oxus River" class="mw-redirect">Oxus</a> rivers. 539 BC, which was the year in which Persian forces defeated the Babylonian army at Opis, marks the end of around four centuries of Mesopotamian domination of the region with the transition from the Neo-Babylonian Period to the Achaemenid Period. Cyrus entered Babylon and presented himself as a traditional Mesopotamian monarch. Subsequent Achaemenid art and iconography reflect the influence of the new political reality on the Mesopotamian tradition.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Achaemenid_Empire_(flat_map).svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Achaemenid_Empire_%28flat_map%29.svg/220px-Achaemenid_Empire_%28flat_map%29.svg.png" width="220" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Achaemenid_Empire_%28flat_map%29.svg/330px-Achaemenid_Empire_%28flat_map%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Achaemenid_Empire_%28flat_map%29.svg/440px-Achaemenid_Empire_%28flat_map%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="672" data-file-height="442"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Achaemenid_Empire_(flat_map).svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> Achaemenid Empire around the time of 
        <a href="/wiki/Darius_I" title="Darius I">Darius I</a> and 
        <a href="/wiki/Xerxes_I" title="Xerxes I">Xerxes I</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>At its greatest extent, the Achaemenid Empire included the modern territories of Iran, <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan" title="Azerbaijan">Azerbaijan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Armenia" title="Armenia">Armenia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(country)" title="Georgia (country)">Georgia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>, much of the <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a> coastal regions, northeastern <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a> and southern <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a> (<a href="/wiki/Thrace" title="Thrace">Thrace</a>), <a href="/wiki/Macedonia_(ancient_kingdom)" title="Macedonia (ancient kingdom)">Macedonia</a> (northern Greece), <a href="/wiki/Paeonia_(kingdom)" title="Paeonia (kingdom)">Paeonia</a> (<a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Macedonia" title="Republic of Macedonia">FYROM</a>), Bulgaria, <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a>, <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">Lebanon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jordan" title="Jordan">Jordan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Palestine_(region)" title="Palestine (region)">Palestine</a>, all significant ancient population centers of <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Egypt" title="Ancient Egypt">ancient Egypt</a> as far west as <a href="/wiki/Libya" title="Libya">Libya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kuwait" title="Kuwait">Kuwait</a>, northern <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a>, parts of the <a href="/wiki/UAE" title="UAE" class="mw-redirect">UAE</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oman" title="Oman">Oman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a>, and much of <a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">Central Asia</a>, making it the first <a href="/wiki/World_government" title="World government">world government</a> and the largest empire it had yet seen.<sup id="cite_ref-book_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-book-22">[22]</a></sup> It is estimated that in 480 BC, 50 million people lived in the Achaemenid Empire.<sup id="cite_ref-1996.2C_p._47_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1996.2C_p._47-71">[70]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Cook_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cook-72">[71]</a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/Guinness_World_Records" title="Guinness World Records">Guinness World Records</a>, the empire at its peak ruled over 44% of the world's population, the highest such figure for any empire in history.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[72]</a></sup> In Greek history, it is considered as the <i>antagonist</i> of the <a href="/wiki/Polis" title="Polis">Greek city states</a>, for the emancipation of slaves including the <a href="/wiki/Jewish_people" title="Jewish people" class="mw-redirect">Jewish</a> <a href="/wiki/Babylonian_captivity" title="Babylonian captivity">exiles in Babylon</a>, building infrastructures such as <a href="/wiki/Royal_road" title="Royal road" class="mw-redirect">road</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chapar_Khaneh" title="Chapar Khaneh">postal</a> systems, and the use of an <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">official language</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Aramaic" title="Imperial Aramaic" class="mw-redirect">Imperial Aramaic</a>, throughout its territories.<sup id="cite_ref-book_22-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-book-22">[22]</a></sup> The empire had a centralized, bureaucratic administration under the emperor, a large professional army, and civil services, inspiring similar developments in later empires.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[73]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-schmitt-EI-i_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-schmitt-EI-i-75">[74]</a></sup> Furthermore, one of the <a href="/wiki/Seven_Wonders_of_the_Ancient_World" title="Seven Wonders of the Ancient World">Seven Wonders of the Ancient World</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Mausoleum_at_Halicarnassus" title="Mausoleum at Halicarnassus">Mausoleum at Halicarnassus</a>, was built in the empire between 353 to 350 BC.</p> 
     <p>Eventual conflict on the western borders began with the <a href="/wiki/Ionian_Revolt" title="Ionian Revolt">Ionian Revolt</a> which erupted into the <a href="/wiki/Greco-Persian_Wars" title="Greco-Persian Wars">Greco-Persian Wars</a>, and continued through the first half of the 5th century BC, and ended with the Persian withdrawal from all of their European territories in the <a href="/wiki/Balkans" title="Balkans">Balkans</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Europe" title="Eastern Europe">Eastern Europe</a> proper.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERoismanWorthington2011135.E2.80.93138.2C_342.E2.80.93345_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERoismanWorthington2011135.E2.80.93138.2C_342.E2.80.93345-76">[75]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>In 334&nbsp;BC, <a href="/wiki/Alexander_the_Great" title="Alexander the Great">Alexander the Great</a> invaded the Achaemenid Empire, defeating the last Achaemenid emperor, <a href="/wiki/Darius_III" title="Darius III">Darius III</a>, at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Issus" title="Battle of Issus">Battle of Issus</a>. Following the premature death of Alexander, Iran came under the control of the <a href="/wiki/Hellenistic" title="Hellenistic" class="mw-redirect">Hellenistic</a> <a href="/wiki/Seleucid_Empire" title="Seleucid Empire">Seleucid Empire</a>. In the middle of the 2nd century BC, the <a href="/wiki/Parthian_Empire" title="Parthian Empire">Parthian Empire</a> rose to become the main power in Iran, and the century-long geopolitical arch-rivalry between Romans and Parthians began, culminating in the <a href="/wiki/Roman%E2%80%93Parthian_Wars" title="Roman–Parthian Wars">Roman–Parthian Wars</a>. The Parthian Empire continued as a feudal monarchy for nearly five centuries, until 224&nbsp;CE, when it was succeeded by the <a href="/wiki/Sassanid_Empire" title="Sassanid Empire" class="mw-redirect">Sassanid Empire</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[76]</a></sup> Together with their neighboring arch-rival, the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman</a>-<a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantines</a>, they made up the world's two most dominant powers at the time, for over four centuries.<sup id="cite_ref-Norman_A._Stillman_p._22_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Norman_A._Stillman_p._22-23">[23]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Byzantine_Studies_2006.2C_p._29_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Byzantine_Studies_2006.2C_p._29-24">[24]</a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Sassanid_reliefs_at_Taq_e_Bostan.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Sassanid_reliefs_at_Taq_e_Bostan.jpg/220px-Sassanid_reliefs_at_Taq_e_Bostan.jpg" width="220" height="224" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Sassanid_reliefs_at_Taq_e_Bostan.jpg/330px-Sassanid_reliefs_at_Taq_e_Bostan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/72/Sassanid_reliefs_at_Taq_e_Bostan.jpg 2x" data-file-width="367" data-file-height="373"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Sassanid_reliefs_at_Taq_e_Bostan.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Sasanian_art" title="Sasanian art">Sassanid reliefs</a> at 
        <a href="/wiki/Taq_Bostan" title="Taq Bostan">Taq Bostan</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The Sassanids established an empire within the frontiers achieved by the Achaemenids, with their capital at <a href="/wiki/Ctesiphon" title="Ctesiphon">Ctesiphon</a>. The Sassanid Empire of the <a href="/wiki/Late_Antiquity" title="Late Antiquity">Late Antiquity</a> is considered as one of the most influential periods of Iran, as Iran influenced the culture of <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_ancient_Rome" title="Culture of ancient Rome">ancient Rome</a> (and through that as far as <a href="/wiki/Western_Europe" title="Western Europe">Western Europe</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-J._B._Bury.2C_p._109_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-J._B._Bury.2C_p._109-78">[77]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[78]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Africa" title="Culture of Africa">Africa</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[79]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Chinese_culture" title="Chinese culture">China</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_India" title="Culture of India">India</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[80]</a></sup> and played a prominent role in the formation of both <a href="/wiki/Medieval_art" title="Medieval art">European</a> and <a href="/wiki/History_of_Eastern_art" title="History of Eastern art" class="mw-redirect">Asian</a> medieval art.<sup id="cite_ref-Iransaga:_The_art_of_Sassanians_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Iransaga:_The_art_of_Sassanians-82">[81]</a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Bas_relief_nagsh-e-rostam_al.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Bas_relief_nagsh-e-rostam_al.jpg/220px-Bas_relief_nagsh-e-rostam_al.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Bas_relief_nagsh-e-rostam_al.jpg/330px-Bas_relief_nagsh-e-rostam_al.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Bas_relief_nagsh-e-rostam_al.jpg/440px-Bas_relief_nagsh-e-rostam_al.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1892" data-file-height="1419"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Bas_relief_nagsh-e-rostam_al.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> A bas-relief at 
        <a href="/wiki/Naqsh-e_Rostam" title="Naqsh-e Rostam" class="mw-redirect">Naqsh-e Rostam</a>, depicting the victory of 
        <a href="/wiki/Shapur_I" title="Shapur I">Shapur I</a> over 
        <a href="/wiki/Valerian_(emperor)" title="Valerian (emperor)">Valerian</a>, following the 
        <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Edessa" title="Battle of Edessa">Battle of Edessa</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Most of the era of both Parthian and Sassanid empires were overshadowed by the <a href="/wiki/Roman-Persian_Wars" title="Roman-Persian Wars" class="mw-redirect">Roman-Persian Wars</a>, which raged on their western borders at the <a href="/wiki/Anatolia" title="Anatolia">Anatolia</a>, the western <a href="/wiki/Caucasus" title="Caucasus">Caucasus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mesopotamia" title="Mesopotamia">Mesopotamia</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Levant" title="Levant">Levant</a>, for over 700 years. These wars exhausted both Romans and Sassanids, and led to the defeat of both at the hands of the invading Muslim Arabs.</p> 
     <p>Several offshoots of the Achaemenids, Parthians, and Sassanids, established <a href="/wiki/Eponymous" title="Eponymous" class="mw-redirect">eponymous</a> dynasties and branches in Anatolia and the Caucasus, including the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Pontus" title="Kingdom of Pontus">Kingdom of Pontus</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Mihranids" title="Mihranids">Mihranids</a>, and the Arsacid dynasties of <a href="/wiki/Arsacid_dynasty_of_Armenia" title="Arsacid dynasty of Armenia">Armenia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arsacid_dynasty_of_Iberia" title="Arsacid dynasty of Iberia">Iberia</a> (<a href="/wiki/Georgia_(country)" title="Georgia (country)">Georgia</a>), and <a href="/wiki/Arsacid_Dynasty_of_Caucasian_Albania" title="Arsacid Dynasty of Caucasian Albania" class="mw-redirect">Caucasian Albania</a> (present-day <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan" title="Azerbaijan">Azerbaijan</a> and southern <a href="/wiki/Dagestan" title="Dagestan">Dagestan</a>).</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Medieval_period">Medieval period</span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles: 
      <a href="/wiki/Muslim_conquest_of_Persia" title="Muslim conquest of Persia">Muslim conquest of Persia</a> and 
      <a href="/wiki/History_of_Iran#Medieval_Iran" title="History of Iran">Medieval Iran</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The prolonged <a href="/wiki/Byzantine-Sassanid_Wars" title="Byzantine-Sassanid Wars" class="mw-redirect">Byzantine-Sassanid Wars</a>, most importantly the climactic <a href="/wiki/Byzantine-Sassanid_War_of_602-628" title="Byzantine-Sassanid War of 602-628" class="mw-redirect">Byzantine-Sassanid War of 602-628</a>, as well as the <a href="/wiki/Fall_of_the_Sassanid_Empire#Social_problems" title="Fall of the Sassanid Empire" class="mw-redirect">social conflict within the Sassanid Empire</a>, opened the way for an Arab invasion to Iran in the 7th century.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[82]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[83]</a></sup> Initially defeated by the Arab <a href="/wiki/Rashidun_Caliphate" title="Rashidun Caliphate">Rashidun Caliphate</a>, Iran came under the rule of the Arab caliphates of <a href="/wiki/Ummayad_Caliphate" title="Ummayad Caliphate" class="mw-redirect">Umayyad</a> and <a href="/wiki/Abbasid_Caliphate" title="Abbasid Caliphate">Abbasid</a>. The prolonged and gradual process of the <a href="/wiki/Islamization_of_Iran" title="Islamization of Iran">Islamization of Iran</a> began following the conquest. Under the new Arab elite of the Rashidun and later the Umayyad caliphates, both converted (<a href="/wiki/Mawali" title="Mawali" class="mw-redirect">mawali</a>) and non-converted (<a href="/wiki/Dhimmi" title="Dhimmi">dhimmi</a>) Iranians were discriminated against, being excluded from the government and military, and having to pay a special tax called <i><a href="/wiki/Jizya" title="Jizya">Jizya</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Hashemi2008_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hashemi2008-85">[84]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[85]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Gundeshapur" title="Gundeshapur">Gunde Shapur</a>, home of the <i><a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Gondishapur" title="Academy of Gondishapur">Academy of Gunde Shapur</a></i> which was the most important medical center of the world at the time, survived after the invasion, but became known as an Islamic institute thereafter.<sup id="cite_ref-rnfrye_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rnfrye-87">[86]</a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Hafez_880714_095.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Hafez_880714_095.jpg/220px-Hafez_880714_095.jpg" width="220" height="154" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Hafez_880714_095.jpg/330px-Hafez_880714_095.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Hafez_880714_095.jpg/440px-Hafez_880714_095.jpg 2x" data-file-width="700" data-file-height="490"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Hafez_880714_095.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> Tomb of 
        <a href="/wiki/Hafez" title="Hafez">Hafez</a>, the popular 
        <a href="/wiki/List_of_Persian_poets_and_authors" title="List of Persian poets and authors">Iranian poet</a> whose works are regarded as a pinnacle in 
        <a href="/wiki/Persian_literature" title="Persian literature">Persian literature</a>, and have left a considerable mark on later Western writers, most notably 
        <a href="/wiki/Goethe" title="Goethe" class="mw-redirect">Goethe</a>, 
        <a href="/wiki/Thoreau" title="Thoreau" class="mw-redirect">Thoreau</a>, and 
        <a href="/wiki/Ralph_Waldo_Emerson" title="Ralph Waldo Emerson">Emerson</a>
        <sup id="cite_ref-Paul_Kane_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Paul_Kane-88">[87]</a></sup>
        <sup id="cite_ref-Shafiq_Shamel_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shafiq_Shamel-89">[88]</a></sup>
        <sup id="cite_ref-Adineh_Khojasteh_Pour_and_Behnam_Mirza_Baba_Zadeh_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Adineh_Khojasteh_Pour_and_Behnam_Mirza_Baba_Zadeh-90">[89]</a></sup>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>In 750, the <a href="/wiki/Abbasids" title="Abbasids" class="mw-redirect">Abbasids</a> overthrew the Umayyads, due mainly to the support from the mawali Iranians.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[90]</a></sup> The mawali formed the majority of the rebel army, which was led by the Iranian general <a href="/wiki/Abu_Muslim" title="Abu Muslim">Abu Muslim</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-wsu_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wsu-92">[91]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[92]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[93]</a></sup> The arrival of the Abbasid Caliphs saw a revival of <a href="/wiki/Iranian_culture" title="Iranian culture" class="mw-redirect">Iranian culture</a> and influence, and a move away from the imposed Arabic customs. The role of the old Arab aristocracy was gradually replaced by an Iranian bureaucracy.<sup id="cite_ref-Mahmud1988_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mahmud1988-95">[94]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>After two centuries of the Arab rule, semi-independent and independent Iranian kingdoms such as the <a href="/wiki/Tahirids" title="Tahirids" class="mw-redirect">Tahirids</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saffarids" title="Saffarids" class="mw-redirect">Saffarids</a>, <a href="/wiki/Samanids" title="Samanids" class="mw-redirect">Samanids</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Buyids" title="Buyids" class="mw-redirect">Buyids</a>, began to appear on the fringes of the declining Abbasid Caliphate. By the Samanid era in the 9th and 10th centuries, the efforts of Iranians to regain their independence had been well solidified.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[95]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>The blossoming <a href="/wiki/Iranian_literature" title="Iranian literature" class="mw-redirect">literature</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iranian_philosophy" title="Iranian philosophy">philosophy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Science_and_technology_in_Iran" title="Science and technology in Iran">medicine</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Iranian_art" title="Iranian art" class="mw-redirect">art</a> of Iran became major elements in the formation of a new age for the Iranian civilization, during the period known as the <i><a href="/wiki/Islamic_Golden_Age" title="Islamic Golden Age">Islamic Golden Age</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[96]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[97]</a></sup> The Islamic Golden Age reached its peak by the 10th and 11th centuries, during which Iran was the main theater of the scientific activities.<sup id="cite_ref-rnfrye_87-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rnfrye-87">[86]</a></sup> After the 10th century, <a href="/wiki/Persian_language" title="Persian language">Persian language</a>, alongside <a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" title="Arabic language" class="mw-redirect">Arabic</a>, was used for the scientific, philosophical, historical, musical, and medical works, whereas the important Iranian writers, such as <a href="/wiki/Nasir_al-Din_al-Tusi" title="Nasir al-Din al-Tusi">Tusi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Avicenna" title="Avicenna">Avicenna</a>, <a href="/wiki/Qotb_al-Din_Shirazi" title="Qotb al-Din Shirazi" class="mw-redirect">Qotb od Din Shirazi</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Biruni" title="Biruni" class="mw-redirect">Biruni</a>, had major contributions in the scientific writing.</p> 
     <p>The cultural revival that began in the Abbasid period led to a resurfacing of the <a href="/wiki/Iranian_nationalism" title="Iranian nationalism">Iranian national identity</a>, and so earlier attempts of <a href="/wiki/Arabization" title="Arabization">Arabization</a> never succeeded in Iran. The Iranian <a href="/wiki/Shuubiyah" title="Shuubiyah" class="mw-redirect">Shuubiyah</a> movement became a catalyst for Iranians to regain independence in their relations with the Arab invaders.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[98]</a></sup> The most notable effect of this movement was the continuation of <a href="/wiki/Persian_language" title="Persian language">Persian language</a> attested to the epic poet <a href="/wiki/Ferdowsi" title="Ferdowsi">Ferdowsi</a>, now regarded as the most important figure in Iranian literature.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Toghrol_Tower_in_Ray.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Toghrol_Tower_in_Ray.jpg/220px-Toghrol_Tower_in_Ray.jpg" width="220" height="235" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Toghrol_Tower_in_Ray.jpg/330px-Toghrol_Tower_in_Ray.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Toghrol_Tower_in_Ray.jpg/440px-Toghrol_Tower_in_Ray.jpg 2x" data-file-width="886" data-file-height="945"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Toghrol_Tower_in_Ray.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Tughrul_Tower" title="Tughrul Tower">Toghrol Tower</a>, a 12th-century monument in 
        <a href="/wiki/Rey,_Iran" title="Rey, Iran">Rey, Iran</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The 10th century saw a mass migration of <a href="/wiki/Turkic_tribes" title="Turkic tribes" class="mw-redirect">Turkic tribes</a> from <a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">Central Asia</a> into the Iranian plateau.<sup id="cite_ref-thePersians_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thePersians-100">[99]</a></sup> Turkic tribesmen were first used in the Abbasid army as <a href="/wiki/Mamluks" title="Mamluks" class="mw-redirect">mamluks</a> (slave-warriors), replacing Iranian and Arab elements within the army.<sup id="cite_ref-wsu_92-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wsu-92">[91]</a></sup> As a result, the mamluks gained a significant political power. In 999, large portions of Iran came briefly under the rule of the <a href="/wiki/Ghaznavids" title="Ghaznavids">Ghaznavids</a>, whose rulers were of mamluk Turk origin, and longer subsequently under the Turkish <a href="/wiki/Seljuk_Empire" title="Seljuk Empire">Seljuk</a> and <a href="/wiki/Khwarezmian_Empire" title="Khwarezmian Empire" class="mw-redirect">Khwarezmian</a> empires. These Turks had been <a href="/wiki/Persianisation" title="Persianisation" class="mw-redirect">Persianized</a> and had adopted Persian models of administration and rulership.<sup id="cite_ref-thePersians_100-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thePersians-100">[99]</a></sup> The Seljuks subsequently gave rise to the <a href="/wiki/Sultanate_of_Rum" title="Sultanate of Rum">Sultanate of Rum</a> in Anatolia, while taking their thoroughly Persianized identity with them.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[100]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[101]</a></sup> The result of the adoption and patronage of <a href="/wiki/Persian_culture" title="Persian culture" class="mw-redirect">Persian culture</a> by Turkish rulers was the development of a distinct <a href="/wiki/Turko-Persian_tradition" title="Turko-Persian tradition">Turko-Persian tradition</a>.</p> 
     <p>In 1219–21 the <a href="/wiki/Khwarezmian_Empire" title="Khwarezmian Empire" class="mw-redirect">Khwarezmian Empire</a> suffered a devastating <a href="/wiki/Invasion" title="Invasion">invasion</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Mongol" title="Mongol" class="mw-redirect">Mongol</a> army of <a href="/wiki/Genghis_Khan" title="Genghis Khan">Genghis Khan</a>. According to Steven R. Ward, "<a href="/wiki/Mongol_conquests" title="Mongol conquests" class="mw-redirect">Mongol violence and depredations</a> killed up to three-fourths of the population of the Iranian Plateau, possibly 10 to 15 million people. Some historians have estimated that Iran's population did not again reach its pre-Mongol levels until the mid-20th century."<sup id="cite_ref-Immortal_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Immortal-103">[102]</a></sup> Following the fracture of the Mongol Empire in 1256, <a href="/wiki/Hulagu_Khan" title="Hulagu Khan">Hulagu Khan</a>, grandson of Genghis Khan, established the <a href="/wiki/Ilkhanate" title="Ilkhanate">Ilkhanate</a> in Iran. In 1370, yet another conqueror, <a href="/wiki/Timur" title="Timur">Timur</a>, followed the example of <a href="/wiki/Hulagu" title="Hulagu" class="mw-redirect">Hulagu</a>, establishing the <a href="/wiki/Timurid_Empire" title="Timurid Empire">Timurid Empire</a> which lasted for another 156 years. In 1387, Timur ordered the complete massacre of <a href="/wiki/Isfahan" title="Isfahan">Isfahan</a>, reportedly killing 70,000 citizens.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[103]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Ilkhans" title="Ilkhans" class="mw-redirect">Ilkhans</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Timurids" title="Timurids" class="mw-redirect">Timurids</a> soon came to adopt the ways and customs of the Iranians, choosing to surround themselves with a culture that was distinctively Iranian.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[104]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_modern_period">Early modern period</span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles: 
      <a href="/wiki/Safavid_Dynasty" title="Safavid Dynasty" class="mw-redirect">Safavid Dynasty</a>, 
      <a href="/wiki/Afsharid_Dynasty" title="Afsharid Dynasty" class="mw-redirect">Afsharid Dynasty</a>, 
      <a href="/wiki/Zand_Dynasty" title="Zand Dynasty" class="mw-redirect">Zand Dynasty</a>, 
      <a href="/wiki/Qajar_Dynasty" title="Qajar Dynasty" class="mw-redirect">Qajar Dynasty</a> and 
      <a href="/wiki/Pahlavi_Dynasty" title="Pahlavi Dynasty" class="mw-redirect">Pahlavi Dynasty</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Shah_Ismail_I.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Shah_Ismail_I.jpg/170px-Shah_Ismail_I.jpg" width="170" height="218" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Shah_Ismail_I.jpg/255px-Shah_Ismail_I.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Shah_Ismail_I.jpg/340px-Shah_Ismail_I.jpg 2x" data-file-width="776" data-file-height="993"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Shah_Ismail_I.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> A 
        <a href="/wiki/Venetian_school_(art)" title="Venetian school (art)">Venetian</a> portrait of 
        <a href="/wiki/Ismail_I" title="Ismail I">Ismail I</a>, founder of the 
        <a href="/wiki/Safavid_Dynasty" title="Safavid Dynasty" class="mw-redirect">Safavid Dynasty</a> – the 
        <a href="/wiki/Uffizi_Gallery" title="Uffizi Gallery" class="mw-redirect">Uffizi Gallery</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>By the <a href="/wiki/1500s_(decade)" title="1500s (decade)">1500s</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ismail_I" title="Ismail I">Ismail I</a> from <a href="/wiki/Ardabil" title="Ardabil">Ardabil</a>, established the <a href="/wiki/Safavid_Dynasty" title="Safavid Dynasty" class="mw-redirect">Safavid Dynasty</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Tabriz" title="Tabriz">Tabriz</a> as the capital.<sup id="cite_ref-thePersians_100-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thePersians-100">[99]</a></sup> Beginning with Azerbaijan, he subsequently extended his authority over all of the Iranian territories, and established an intermittent Iranian hegemony over the vast relative regions, reasserting the Iranian identity within large parts of the <a href="/wiki/Greater_Iran" title="Greater Iran">Greater Iran</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[105]</a></sup> Iran was predominantly <a href="/wiki/Sunni" title="Sunni" class="mw-redirect">Sunni</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Abdullah2014_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Abdullah2014-107">[106]</a></sup> but Ismail instigated a <a href="/wiki/Safavid_conversion_of_Iran_from_Sunnism_to_Shiism" title="Safavid conversion of Iran from Sunnism to Shiism" class="mw-redirect">forced conversion</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Shia" title="Shia" class="mw-redirect">Shia</a> branch of Islam,<sup id="cite_ref-BBCReligion_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCReligion-108">[107]</a></sup> by which the Shia Islam spread throughout the Safavid territories in the <a href="/wiki/Caucasus" title="Caucasus">Caucasus</a>, Iran, <a href="/wiki/Anatolia" title="Anatolia">Anatolia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mesopotamia" title="Mesopotamia">Mesopotamia</a>. As a result, thereof, the modern-day Iran is the only official Shia nation of the world, with it holding an absolute majority in Iran and the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Azerbaijan" title="Republic of Azerbaijan" class="mw-redirect">Republic of Azerbaijan</a>, having there the 1st and 2nd highest number of Shia inhabitants by population percentage in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[108]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-books.google.com.au_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-books.google.com.au-110">[109]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>The centuries-long geopolitical and ideological rivalry between Safavid Iran and the neighboring <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a>, led to numerous <a href="/wiki/Ottoman%E2%80%93Persian_Wars" title="Ottoman–Persian Wars">Ottoman–Persian Wars</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Immortal_103-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Immortal-103">[102]</a></sup> The Safavid Era peaked in the reign of <a href="/wiki/Abbas_the_Great" title="Abbas the Great" class="mw-redirect">Abbas the Great</a>, 1587–1629,<sup id="cite_ref-Immortal_103-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Immortal-103">[102]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FattahCaso2009_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FattahCaso2009-111">[110]</a></sup> surpassing their Ottoman arch rivals in strength, and making the empire a leading hub in Western Eurasia for the sciences and arts. The Safavid Era saw the start of mass integration from <a href="/wiki/Peoples_of_the_Caucasus" title="Peoples of the Caucasus">Caucasian populations</a> into new layers of the society of Iran, as well as mass resettlement of them within the heartlands of Iran, playing a pivotal role in the history of Iran for centuries onwards. Following a gradual decline in the late 1600s and early 1700s, which was caused by the internal conflicts, the continuous wars with the Ottomans, and the foreign interference (most notably the Russian interference), the Safavid rule was ended by the <a href="/wiki/Hotaki_dynasty" title="Hotaki dynasty" class="mw-redirect">Pashtun rebels</a> who besieged Isfahan and defeated <a href="/wiki/Soltan_Hosein" title="Soltan Hosein" class="mw-redirect">Soltan Hosein</a> in 1722.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Nader_Shah_Statue_in_Mashhad.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Nader_Shah_Statue_in_Mashhad.jpg/220px-Nader_Shah_Statue_in_Mashhad.jpg" width="220" height="132" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Nader_Shah_Statue_in_Mashhad.jpg/330px-Nader_Shah_Statue_in_Mashhad.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Nader_Shah_Statue_in_Mashhad.jpg/440px-Nader_Shah_Statue_in_Mashhad.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3504" data-file-height="2107"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Nader_Shah_Statue_in_Mashhad.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> Statue of 
        <a href="/wiki/Nader_Shah" title="Nader Shah">Nader Shah</a>, founder of the 
        <a href="/wiki/Afsharid_Dynasty" title="Afsharid Dynasty" class="mw-redirect">Afsharid Dynasty</a> – the Naderi Museum
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>In 1729, <a href="/wiki/Nader_Shah" title="Nader Shah">Nader Shah</a>, a chieftain and military genius from <a href="/wiki/Greater_Khorasan" title="Greater Khorasan">Khorasan</a>, successfully drove out and conquered the Pashtun invaders. He subsequently took back the annexed Caucasian territories which <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Constantinople_(1724)" title="Treaty of Constantinople (1724)">were divided</a> among the Ottoman and <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Russia" title="Imperial Russia" class="mw-redirect">Russian</a> authorities by the ongoing chaos in Iran. During the reign of Nader Shah, Iran reached its greatest extent since the Sassanid Empire, reestablishing the Iranian hegemony all over the <a href="/wiki/Caucasus" title="Caucasus">Caucasus</a>, as well as other major parts of the <a href="/wiki/West_Asia" title="West Asia" class="mw-redirect">west</a> and <a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">central</a> Asia, and briefly possessing what was arguably the most powerful empire at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-books.google.nl_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-books.google.nl-27">[27]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Nader Shah <a href="/wiki/Sack_of_Delhi" title="Sack of Delhi" class="mw-redirect">invaded India and sacked far off Delhi</a> by the late 1730s. His territorial expansion, as well as his military successes, went into a decline following the final <a href="/wiki/Nader%27s_Dagestan_campaign" title="Nader's Dagestan campaign">campaigns in the Northern Caucasus</a>. The assassination of Nader Shah sparked a brief period of civil war and turmoil, after which <a href="/wiki/Karim_Khan" title="Karim Khan">Karim Khan</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Zand_Dynasty" title="Zand Dynasty" class="mw-redirect">Zand Dynasty</a> came to power in 1750, bringing a period of relative peace and prosperity.<sup id="cite_ref-Immortal_103-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Immortal-103">[102]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>The geopolitical reach of the Zand Dynasty was limited, compared to its preceding dynasties, and many of the Iranian territories in the Caucasus gained <i>de facto</i> independence, and were locally ruled through various <a href="/wiki/Khanates_of_the_Caucasus" title="Khanates of the Caucasus">Caucasian khanates</a>. However, despite the self-ruling, they all remained <a href="/wiki/Commoners" title="Commoners" class="mw-redirect">subjects</a> and vassals to the Zand king.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[111]</a></sup> The khanates exercised control over their affairs via international trade routes between Central Asia and the West.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[112]</a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Gulistan-Treaty.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Gulistan-Treaty.jpg/220px-Gulistan-Treaty.jpg" width="220" height="169" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Gulistan-Treaty.jpg/330px-Gulistan-Treaty.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Gulistan-Treaty.jpg/440px-Gulistan-Treaty.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1565" data-file-height="1200"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Gulistan-Treaty.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> Map showing the northwestern borders of Iran in the 19th century, comprising modern-day Eastern 
        <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(country)" title="Georgia (country)">Georgia</a>, 
        <a href="/wiki/Dagestan" title="Dagestan">Dagestan</a>, 
        <a href="/wiki/Armenia" title="Armenia">Armenia</a>, and 
        <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan" title="Azerbaijan">Azerbaijan</a>, before being ceded to neighbouring 
        <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Russia" title="Imperial Russia" class="mw-redirect">Imperial Russia</a> by the 
        <a href="/wiki/Russo-Persian_Wars" title="Russo-Persian Wars">Russo-Persian Wars</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Another civil war ensued after the death of Karim Khan in 1779, out of which <a href="/wiki/Mohammad_Khan_Qajar" title="Mohammad Khan Qajar">Aqa Mohammad Khan</a> emerged, founding the <a href="/wiki/Qajar_Dynasty" title="Qajar Dynasty" class="mw-redirect">Qajar Dynasty</a> in 1794. In 1795, following the disobedience of the <a href="/wiki/Georgians" title="Georgians">Georgian</a> subjects and their <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Georgievsk" title="Treaty of Georgievsk">alliance with the Russians</a>, the Qajars captured <a href="/wiki/Tblisi" title="Tblisi" class="mw-redirect">Tblisi</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Krtsanisi" title="Battle of Krtsanisi">Battle of Krtsanisi</a>, and drove the Russians out of the entire Caucasus, reestablishing a short-lived Iranian <a href="/wiki/Suzerainty" title="Suzerainty">suzerainty</a> over the region. The Russo-Persian wars of <a href="/wiki/Russo-Persian_War_(1804%E2%80%9313)" title="Russo-Persian War (1804–13)">1804–1813</a> and <a href="/wiki/Russo-Persian_War_(1826%E2%80%9328)" title="Russo-Persian War (1826–28)">1826–1828</a> however resulted in large irrevocable territorial losses for Iran in the <a href="/wiki/Caucasus" title="Caucasus">Caucasus</a>, comprising all of <a href="/wiki/Transcaucasia" title="Transcaucasia">Transcaucasia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dagestan" title="Dagestan">Dagestan</a>, which made part of the very concept of Iran for centuries,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFisherAveryHamblyMelville1991329.E2.80.93330_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFisherAveryHamblyMelville1991329.E2.80.93330-28">[28]</a></sup> and thus substantial gains for the neighboring <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a>.
