As a result of the 19th century Russo-Persian wars, the Russians took over the Caucasus, and Iran irrevocably lost control over its integral territories in the region (comprising modern-day Dagestan, <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(country)" title="Georgia (country)">Georgia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Armenia" title="Armenia">Armenia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan" title="Azerbaijan">Azerbaijan</a>), which got confirmed per the treaties of <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Gulistan" title="Treaty of Gulistan">Gulistan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Turkmenchay" title="Treaty of Turkmenchay">Turkmenchay</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Timothy_C._Dowling_pp._728-730_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Timothy_C._Dowling_pp._728-730-29">[29]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[113]</a></sup> The area to the north of the river <a href="/wiki/Aras_River" title="Aras River" class="mw-redirect">Aras</a>, among which the contemporary Republic of Azerbaijan, eastern Georgia, Dagestan, and Armenia, were Iranian territory until they were occupied by Russia in the course of the 19th century.<sup id="cite_ref-Timothy_C._Dowling_pp._728-730_29-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Timothy_C._Dowling_pp._728-730-29">[29]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Swietochowski_Borderland_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Swietochowski_Borderland-115">[114]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[115]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[116]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[117]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[118]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[119]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>As Iran shrank, many <a href="/wiki/Transcaucasus" title="Transcaucasus" class="mw-redirect">Transcaucasian</a> and <a href="/wiki/North_Caucasus" title="North Caucasus">North Caucasian</a> Muslims moved towards Iran,<sup id="cite_ref-Mansoori_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mansoori-121">[120]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-122">[121]</a></sup> especially until the aftermath <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_Cleansing_of_Circassians" title="Ethnic Cleansing of Circassians" class="mw-redirect">result of the Caucasian War</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_122-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-122">[121]</a></sup> and the decades afterwards, while Iran's Armenians were encouraged to settle in the newly incorporated Russian territories,<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[122]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[123]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[124]</a></sup> causing significant demographic shifts.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Late_modern_period">Late modern period</span></h3> 
     <table class="metadata plainlinks ambox ambox-style ambox-Context" role="presentation"> 
      <tbody>
       <tr> 
        <td class="mbox-image"> 
         <div style="width:52px">
          <img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f2/Edit-clear.svg/40px-Edit-clear.svg.png" width="40" height="40" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f2/Edit-clear.svg/60px-Edit-clear.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f2/Edit-clear.svg/80px-Edit-clear.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="48" data-file-height="48">
         </div> </td> 
        <td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span">This article <b>provides insufficient context for those unfamiliar with the subject</b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Iran&amp;action=edit">improve the article</a> with a <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Writing_better_articles#Lead_section" title="Wikipedia:Writing better articles">good introductory style</a>.</span> <small><i>(March 2016)</i></small></span></td> 
       </tr> 
      </tbody>
     </table> 
     <p>Around 1.5 million people—20 to 25% of the population of Iran—died as a result of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_famines" title="List of famines">Great Famine of 1870–1871</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[125]</a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Parliamenttehran.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Parliamenttehran.jpg/220px-Parliamenttehran.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Parliamenttehran.jpg/330px-Parliamenttehran.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Parliamenttehran.jpg/440px-Parliamenttehran.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Parliamenttehran.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> The first national 
        <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Iran" title="Parliament of Iran" class="mw-redirect">parliament of Iran</a>, established in 1906
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Between 1872 and 1905, a series of protests took place in response to the sale of <a href="/wiki/Concession_(contract)" title="Concession (contract)">concessions</a> to foreigners by <a href="/wiki/Nasser_al-Din_Shah" title="Nasser al-Din Shah" class="mw-redirect">Nasser od Din</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mozaffar_ad-Din_Shah" title="Mozaffar ad-Din Shah" class="mw-redirect">Mozaffar od Din</a> shahs of <a href="/wiki/Qajar" title="Qajar" class="mw-redirect">Qajar</a>, and led to the <a href="/wiki/Iranian_Constitutional_Revolution" title="Iranian Constitutional Revolution" class="mw-redirect">Iranian Constitutional Revolution</a>. The first <a href="/wiki/Persian_Constitution_of_1906" title="Persian Constitution of 1906">Iranian Constitution</a> and the first <a href="/wiki/Majles" title="Majles" class="mw-redirect">national parliament of Iran</a> were founded in 1906, through the ongoing revolution. The Constitution included the official recognition of Iran's three religious minorities, namely <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zoroastrianism" title="Zoroastrianism">Zoroastrians</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Judaism" title="Judaism">Jews</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Colin_Brock_p_99_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Colin_Brock_p_99-127">[126]</a></sup> which has remained a basis in the legislation of Iran since then.</p> 
     <p>The struggle related to the constitutional movement continued until 1911, when <a href="/wiki/Mohammad_Ali_Shah" title="Mohammad Ali Shah" class="mw-redirect">Mohammad Ali Shah</a> was defeated and forced to abdicate. On the pretext of restoring order, the Russians occupied Northern Iran in 1911, and maintained a military presence in the region for years to come. During <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, the British occupied much of Western Iran, and fully withdrew in 1921. The <a href="/wiki/Persian_Campaign" title="Persian Campaign">Persian Campaign</a> commenced furthermore during World War I in Northwestern Iran after an Ottoman invasion, as part of the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Eastern_Theatre_of_World_War_I" title="Middle Eastern Theatre of World War I" class="mw-redirect">Middle Eastern Theatre of World War I</a>. As a result of Ottoman hostilities across the border, a large amount of the Assyrians of Iran <a href="/wiki/Assyrian_Genocide" title="Assyrian Genocide" class="mw-redirect">were massacred</a> by the Ottoman armies, notably in and around <a href="/wiki/Urmia" title="Urmia">Urmia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-128">[127]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Alexander_Laban_Hinton_p._117_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Alexander_Laban_Hinton_p._117-129">[128]</a></sup> Apart from the rule of Aqa Mohammad Khan, the Qajar rule is characterized as a century of misrule.<sup id="cite_ref-thePersians_100-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thePersians-100">[99]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>In 1921, the <a href="/wiki/Qajar_Dynasty" title="Qajar Dynasty" class="mw-redirect">Qajar Dynasty</a> <a href="/wiki/1921_Persian_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="1921 Persian coup d'état">was overthrown</a> by <a href="/wiki/Reza_Khan" title="Reza Khan" class="mw-redirect">Reza Khan</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Pahlavi_Dynasty" title="Pahlavi Dynasty" class="mw-redirect">Pahlavi Dynasty</a>, who was the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Prime_Ministers_of_Iran" title="List of Prime Ministers of Iran">Prime Minister of Iran</a> and the former general of the <a href="/wiki/Persian_Cossack_Brigade" title="Persian Cossack Brigade">Persian Cossack Brigade</a>, and he became the new <a href="/wiki/Shah" title="Shah">Shah</a>.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Mohammad_Pahlavi_Coronation.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Mohammad_Pahlavi_Coronation.jpg/220px-Mohammad_Pahlavi_Coronation.jpg" width="220" height="294" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/20/Mohammad_Pahlavi_Coronation.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/20/Mohammad_Pahlavi_Coronation.jpg 2x" data-file-width="329" data-file-height="440"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Mohammad_Pahlavi_Coronation.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Mohammad_Reza_Pahlavi" title="Mohammad Reza Pahlavi">Mohammad Reza Pahlavi</a> and the Imperial Family in the Coronation of the Shah of Iran, 1967
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>In 1941, Reza Shah was forced to abdicate in favor of his son, <a href="/wiki/Mohammad_Reza_Pahlavi" title="Mohammad Reza Pahlavi">Mohammad Reza Pahlavi</a>, and established the <a href="/wiki/Persian_Corridor" title="Persian Corridor">Persian Corridor</a>, a massive supply route that would last until the end of the ongoing war. The presence of so many foreign troops in the nation also culminated in the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet-backed</a> establishment of two puppet regimes in the nation; the <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan_People%27s_Government" title="Azerbaijan People's Government">Azerbaijan People's Government</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Mahabad" title="Republic of Mahabad">Republic of Mahabad</a>. As the Soviet Union refused to relinquish the occupied Iranian territory, the <a href="/wiki/Iran_crisis_of_1946" title="Iran crisis of 1946">Iran crisis of 1946</a> was followed, which particularly resulted in the dissolution of both puppet states, and the withdrawal of the Soviets.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Mossadeghmohammad.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Mossadeghmohammad.jpg/170px-Mossadeghmohammad.jpg" width="170" height="218" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Mossadeghmohammad.jpg/255px-Mossadeghmohammad.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e9/Mossadeghmohammad.jpg 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="384"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Mossadeghmohammad.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Mohammad_Mosaddegh" title="Mohammad Mosaddegh">Mohammad Mosaddegh</a>, democracy advocate and deposed 
        <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Iran" title="Prime Minister of Iran">Prime Minister of Iran</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>In 1951, <a href="/wiki/Mohammad_Mosaddegh" title="Mohammad Mosaddegh">Mohammad Mosaddegh</a> was elected as the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Iran" title="Prime Minister of Iran">prime minister</a>. He became enormously popular in Iran, after he <a href="/wiki/Nationalize" title="Nationalize" class="mw-redirect">nationalized</a> <a href="/wiki/Petroleum_industry_in_Iran" title="Petroleum industry in Iran">Iran's petroleum industry</a> and oil reserves. He was deposed in the <a href="/wiki/1953_Iranian_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="1953 Iranian coup d'état">1953 Iranian coup d'état</a>, an Anglo-American covert operation that marked the first time the US had overthrown a foreign government during the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Kinzer2011_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kinzer2011-130">[129]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>After the coup, the Shah became increasingly <a href="/wiki/Autocracy" title="Autocracy">autocratic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sultanism" title="Sultanism">sultanistic</a>, and Iran entered a phase of decades long <a href="/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93United_States_relations" title="Iran–United States relations">controversial close relations</a> with the United States and some other foreign governments.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[130]</a></sup> While the Shah increasingly modernized Iran and claimed to retain it as a fully <a href="/wiki/Secular_state" title="Secular state">secular state</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Anthony_H._Cordesman_p_22_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Anthony_H._Cordesman_p_22-30">[30]</a></sup> arbitrary arrests and torture by his secret police, the <a href="/wiki/SAVAK" title="SAVAK">SAVAK</a>, were used to crush all forms of political opposition.</p> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Ayatollah" title="Ayatollah">Ayatollah</a> <a href="/wiki/Ruhollah_Khomeini" title="Ruhollah Khomeini">Ruhollah Khomeini</a> became an active critic of the Shah's <a href="/wiki/White_Revolution" title="White Revolution">White Revolution</a>, and publicly denounced the government. Khomeini was arrested and imprisoned for 18 months. After his release in 1964, Khomeini publicly criticized the United States government. The Shah sent him into exile. He went first to Turkey, then to Iraq, and finally to France.</p> 
     <p>Due to the <a href="/wiki/1973_oil_crisis" title="1973 oil crisis">1973 spike in oil prices</a>, the economy of Iran was flooded with foreign currency, which caused <a href="/wiki/Inflation" title="Inflation">inflation</a>. By 1974, the economy of Iran was experiencing double digit inflation, and despite many large projects to modernize the country, corruption was rampant and caused <a href="/wiki/Background_and_causes_of_the_Iranian_Revolution#1970.E2.80.931975" title="Background and causes of the Iranian Revolution">large amounts of waste</a>. By 1975 and 1976, an <a href="/wiki/Economic_recession" title="Economic recession" class="mw-redirect">economic recession</a> led to increased unemployment, especially among millions of youth who had migrated to the cities of Iran looking for construction jobs during the boom years of the early 1970s. By the late 1970s, many of these people opposed the Shah's regime and began to organize and join the protests against it.<sup id="cite_ref-Hurd2009_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hurd2009-132">[131]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="After_the_1979_Revolution">After the 1979 Revolution</span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote">
      See also: 
      <a href="/wiki/1979_Revolution" title="1979 Revolution" class="mw-redirect">1979 Revolution</a> and 
      <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Islamic_Republic_of_Iran" title="History of the Islamic Republic of Iran">History of the Islamic Republic of Iran</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Imam_Khomeini_in_Mehrabad.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Imam_Khomeini_in_Mehrabad.jpg/170px-Imam_Khomeini_in_Mehrabad.jpg" width="170" height="224" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Imam_Khomeini_in_Mehrabad.jpg/255px-Imam_Khomeini_in_Mehrabad.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Imam_Khomeini_in_Mehrabad.jpg/340px-Imam_Khomeini_in_Mehrabad.jpg 2x" data-file-width="573" data-file-height="755"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Imam_Khomeini_in_Mehrabad.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Ruhollah_Khomeini" title="Ruhollah Khomeini">Ruhollah Khomeini</a> 
        <a href="/wiki/Ruhollah_Khomeini%27s_return_to_Iran" title="Ruhollah Khomeini's return to Iran">returning to Iran</a> after 14 years exile, on February 1, 1979
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/1979_Revolution" title="1979 Revolution" class="mw-redirect">1979 Revolution</a>, later known as the <i>Islamic Revolution</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[132]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[133]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[134]</a></sup> began in January 1978 with the first major demonstrations against the Shah.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[135]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>After a year of <a href="/wiki/Iranian_Revolution#General_strike.2C_increasing_opposition.2C_and_military_government" title="Iranian Revolution">strikes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Iranian_Revolution#Renewed_protests" title="Iranian Revolution">demonstrations</a> paralyzing the country and its economy, <a href="/wiki/Iranian_Revolution#The_Shah.27s_exile_and_Khomeini.27s_return" title="Iranian Revolution">Mohammad Reza Pahlavi fled the country and Ruhollah Khomeini returned</a> from exile to Tehran in February 1979, forming a new government.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_this_day_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_this_day-137">[136]</a></sup> After holding a <a href="/wiki/Iranian_Islamic_Republic_referendum,_March_1979" title="Iranian Islamic Republic referendum, March 1979">referendum</a>, in April 1979, Iran officially became an <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Republic" title="Islamic Republic" class="mw-redirect">Islamic Republic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-JohnsonUradnik2011_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JohnsonUradnik2011-138">[137]</a></sup> A second <a href="/wiki/Iranian_constitutional_referendum,_December_1979" title="Iranian constitutional referendum, December 1979">referendum</a> in December 1979 approved a <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_the_Islamic_Republic_of_Iran" title="Constitution of the Islamic Republic of Iran">theocratic constitution</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[138]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>The immediate nationwide uprisings against the new government began by the <a href="/wiki/1979_Kurdish_rebellion_in_Iran" title="1979 Kurdish rebellion in Iran">1979 Kurdish rebellion</a> with the <a href="/wiki/1979_Khuzestan_uprising" title="1979 Khuzestan uprising">Khuzestan uprisings</a>, along with the uprisings in <a href="/wiki/Sistan_and_Baluchestan_Province" title="Sistan and Baluchestan Province">Sistan and Baluchestan Province</a> and other areas. Over the next several years, these uprisings were subdued in a violent manner by <a href="/wiki/Consolidation_of_the_Iranian_Revolution" title="Consolidation of the Iranian Revolution">the new Islamic government</a>. The new government went about <a href="/wiki/Consolidation_of_the_Iranian_Revolution#Suppression_of_opposition" title="Consolidation of the Iranian Revolution">purging itself of the non-Islamist political opposition</a>. Although both nationalists and Marxists had initially joined with Islamists to overthrow the Shah, tens of thousands were executed by the Islamic government afterward.<sup id="cite_ref-Benard_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Benard-140">[139]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>On November 4, 1979, <a href="/wiki/Muslim_Student_Followers_of_the_Imam%27s_Line" title="Muslim Student Followers of the Imam's Line">a group of students</a> seized the United States Embassy and <a href="/wiki/Iran_hostage_crisis" title="Iran hostage crisis">took the embassy with 52 personnel and citizens hostage</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-carterpbs_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-carterpbs-141">[140]</a></sup> after the United States refused to return Mohammad Reza Pahlavi to Iran to face trial in the court of the new regime. Attempts by the <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Carter" title="Jimmy Carter">Jimmy Carter</a> administration to <a href="/wiki/Iran_hostage_crisis_negotiations" title="Iran hostage crisis negotiations">negotiate for the release of the hostages</a>, and a failed <a href="/wiki/Operation_Eagle_Claw" title="Operation Eagle Claw">rescue attempt</a>, helped force Carter out of office and brought <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Reagan" title="Ronald Reagan">Ronald Reagan</a> to power. On Jimmy Carter's final day in office, the last hostages were finally set free as a result of the <a href="/wiki/Algiers_Accords" title="Algiers Accords">Algiers Accords</a>.</p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Iranian_Cultural_Revolution" title="Iranian Cultural Revolution">Cultural Revolution</a> began in 1980, with an initial closure of universities for three years, in order to perform an inspection and cleanup in the cultural policy of the education and training system.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-142">[141]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>On September 22, 1980, the Iraqi army <a href="/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Iraq_War#1980:_Iraqi_invasion" title="Iran–Iraq War">invaded the Iranian Khuzestan</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Iraq_War" title="Iran–Iraq War">Iran–Iraq War</a> began. Although the forces of Saddam Hussein made several early advances, by mid 1982, the Iranian forces successfully managed to <a href="/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Iraq_War#1982:_Iraqi_retreat.2C_Iranian_offensive" title="Iran–Iraq War">drive the Iraqi army back</a> into Iraq. In July 1982, with Iraq thrown on the defensive, Iran took the decision to invade Iraq and conducted countless offensives in a bid to conquer Iraqi territory and capture cities, such as Basra. The war continued until 1988, when the Iraqi army defeated the Iranian forces inside Iraq and pushed the remaining Iranian troops back across the border. Subsequently, Khomeini accepted a <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_598" title="United Nations Security Council Resolution 598">truce mediated by the UN</a>. The total Iranian casualties in the war were estimated to be 123,220–160,000 <a href="/wiki/Killed_in_action" title="Killed in action">KIA</a>, 60,711 <a href="/wiki/Missing_in_action" title="Missing in action">MIA</a>, and 11,000–16,000 <a href="/wiki/Civilian_casualties" title="Civilian casualties">civilians killed</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[142]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[143]</a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:6th_Day_-_Green_Condolence.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/6th_Day_-_Green_Condolence.jpg/220px-6th_Day_-_Green_Condolence.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/6th_Day_-_Green_Condolence.jpg/330px-6th_Day_-_Green_Condolence.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/6th_Day_-_Green_Condolence.jpg/440px-6th_Day_-_Green_Condolence.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2128" data-file-height="1416"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:6th_Day_-_Green_Condolence.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> 
        <i>Silent Demonstration</i> – the 
        <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_Iranian_election_protests" title="2009–10 Iranian election protests" class="mw-redirect">2009–10 Iranian election protests</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Following the Iran–Iraq War, in 1989, <a href="/wiki/Akbar_Hashemi_Rafsanjani" title="Akbar Hashemi Rafsanjani">Akbar Hashemi Rafsanjani</a> and his administration concentrated on a pragmatic pro-business policy of rebuilding and strengthening the economy without making any dramatic break with the ideology of the revolution. In 1997, Rafsanjani was succeeded by the moderate <a href="/wiki/Iranian_reform_movement" title="Iranian reform movement" class="mw-redirect">reformist</a> <a href="/wiki/Mohammad_Khatami" title="Mohammad Khatami">Mohammad Khatami</a>, whose government attempted, unsuccessfully, to make the country more free and democratic.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated3_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated3-145">[144]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Iranian_presidential_election,_2005" title="Iranian presidential election, 2005">2005 presidential election</a> brought conservative populist candidate, <a href="/wiki/Mahmoud_Ahmadinejad" title="Mahmoud Ahmadinejad">Mahmoud Ahmadinejad</a>, to power.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[145]</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/Iranian_presidential_election,_2009" title="Iranian presidential election, 2009">2009 Iranian presidential election</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Interior_(Iran)" title="Ministry of Interior (Iran)">Interior Ministry</a> announced incumbent president Ahmadinejad had won 62.63% of the vote, while <a href="/wiki/Mir-Hossein_Mousavi" title="Mir-Hossein Mousavi">Mir-Hossein Mousavi</a> had come in second place with 33.75%.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[146]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-The_Guardian_November_29_2015c_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Guardian_November_29_2015c-148">[147]</a></sup> Allegations of large irregularities and fraud provoked the <a href="/wiki/2009_Iranian_presidential_election_protests" title="2009 Iranian presidential election protests">2009 Iranian presidential election protests</a>, both within Iran and in major cites outside the country.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[148]</a></sup></p> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Hassan_Rouhani" title="Hassan Rouhani">Hassan Rouhani</a> was elected as <a href="/wiki/President_of_Iran" title="President of Iran">President of Iran</a> on June 15, 2013, defeating <a href="/wiki/Mohammad_Bagher_Ghalibaf" title="Mohammad Bagher Ghalibaf">Mohammad Bagher Ghalibaf</a> and four other candidates.<sup id="cite_ref-BBCannouncedwinner_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCannouncedwinner-150">[149]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-WSJannouncedwinner_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WSJannouncedwinner-151">[150]</a></sup> The electoral victory of new Iranian President Hassan Rouhani has improved the relations of Iran with other countries.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[151]</a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span></h2> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Iran" title="Geography of Iran">Geography of Iran</a>
     </div> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote">
      See also: 
      <a href="/wiki/Agriculture_in_Iran" title="Agriculture in Iran">Agriculture in Iran</a> and 
      <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_Iran" title="Wildlife of Iran">Wildlife of Iran</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Provinces_of_Iran_by_area_(km2).svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Provinces_of_Iran_by_area_%28km2%29.svg/300px-Provinces_of_Iran_by_area_%28km2%29.svg.png" width="300" height="267" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Provinces_of_Iran_by_area_%28km2%29.svg/450px-Provinces_of_Iran_by_area_%28km2%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Provinces_of_Iran_by_area_%28km2%29.svg/600px-Provinces_of_Iran_by_area_%28km2%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="800"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Provinces_of_Iran_by_area_(km2).svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> Provinces of Iran by area (km
        <sup>2</sup>)
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Iran is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_and_dependencies_by_area" title="List of countries and dependencies by area" class="mw-redirect">18th largest country</a> in the world, with an area of 1,648,195&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (636,372&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi).<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-34">[34]</a></sup> Its area roughly equals that of the United Kingdom, France, Spain, and Germany combined, or somewhat more than the US state of <a href="/wiki/Alaska" title="Alaska">Alaska</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[152]</a></sup> Iran lies between latitudes <a href="/wiki/24th_parallel_north" title="24th parallel north">24°</a> and <a href="/wiki/40th_parallel_north" title="40th parallel north">40° N</a>, and longitudes <a href="/wiki/44th_meridian_east" title="44th meridian east">44°</a> and <a href="/wiki/64th_meridian_east" title="64th meridian east">64° E</a>. Its borders are with <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan" title="Azerbaijan">Azerbaijan</a> (611&nbsp;km or 380&nbsp;mi, with <a href="/wiki/Nakhchivan_Autonomous_Republic" title="Nakhchivan Autonomous Republic">Azerbaijan-Naxcivan</a> exclave, 179&nbsp;km or 111&nbsp;mi)<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[153]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Armenia" title="Armenia">Armenia</a> (35&nbsp;km or 22&nbsp;mi) to the north-west; the <a href="/wiki/Caspian_Sea" title="Caspian Sea">Caspian Sea</a> to the north; <a href="/wiki/Turkmenistan" title="Turkmenistan">Turkmenistan</a> (992&nbsp;km or 616&nbsp;mi) to the north-east; <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a> (909&nbsp;km or 565&nbsp;mi) and <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a> (936&nbsp;km or 582&nbsp;mi) to the east; <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> (499&nbsp;km or 310&nbsp;mi) and Iraq (1,458&nbsp;km or 906&nbsp;mi) to the west; and finally the waters of the Persian Gulf and the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Oman" title="Gulf of Oman">Gulf of Oman</a> to the south.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Damavand3.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Damavand3.jpg/220px-Damavand3.jpg" width="220" height="223" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Damavand3.jpg/330px-Damavand3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/d9/Damavand3.jpg 2x" data-file-width="355" data-file-height="360"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Damavand3.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Mount_Damavand" title="Mount Damavand">Mount Damavand</a>, Iran's highest point, is located in 
        <a href="/wiki/Amol_County" title="Amol County">Amol County</a>, 
        <a href="/wiki/Mazanderan" title="Mazanderan" class="mw-redirect">Mazanderan</a>.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Iran consists of the <a href="/wiki/Iranian_Plateau" title="Iranian Plateau">Iranian Plateau</a> with the exception of the coasts of the Caspian Sea and <a href="/wiki/Khuzestan_Province" title="Khuzestan Province">Khuzestan Province</a>. It is one of the world's most mountainous countries, its landscape dominated by rugged <a href="/wiki/Mountain_range" title="Mountain range">mountain ranges</a> that separate various <a href="/wiki/Drainage_basin" title="Drainage basin">basins</a> or <a href="/wiki/Plateau" title="Plateau">plateaux</a> from one another. The populous western part is the most mountainous, with ranges such as the <a href="/wiki/Caucasus_Mountains" title="Caucasus Mountains">Caucasus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zagros_Mountains" title="Zagros Mountains">Zagros</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alborz" title="Alborz">Alborz</a> Mountains; the last contains Iran's highest point, <a href="/wiki/Mount_Damavand" title="Mount Damavand">Mount Damavand</a> at 5,610&nbsp;m (18,406&nbsp;ft), which is also the highest mountain on the Eurasian landmass west of the <a href="/wiki/Hindu_Kush" title="Hindu Kush">Hindu Kush</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[154]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>The northern part of Iran is covered by dense rain forests called <a href="/wiki/Caspian_Hyrcanian_mixed_forests" title="Caspian Hyrcanian mixed forests">Shomal</a> or the Jungles of Iran.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The eastern part consists mostly of <a href="/wiki/Desert" title="Desert">desert</a> basins such as the <a href="/wiki/Dasht-e_Kavir" title="Dasht-e Kavir">Dasht-e Kavir</a>, Iran's largest desert, in the north-central portion of the country, and the <a href="/wiki/Dasht-e_Lut" title="Dasht-e Lut" class="mw-redirect">Dasht-e Lut</a>, in the east, as well as some <a href="/wiki/Salt_lake" title="Salt lake">salt lakes</a>. This is because the mountain ranges are too high for rain clouds to reach these regions.</p> 
     <p>The only large <a href="/wiki/Plain" title="Plain">plains</a> are found along the coast of the Caspian Sea and at the northern end of the Persian Gulf, where Iran borders the mouth of the <a href="/wiki/Shatt_al-Arab" title="Shatt al-Arab">Arvand river</a>. Smaller, discontinuous plains are found along the remaining coast of the Persian Gulf, the <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Hormuz" title="Strait of Hormuz">Strait of Hormuz</a> and the Gulf of Oman.</p>

     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote">
      See also: 
      <a href="/wiki/Environmental_issues_in_Iran" title="Environmental issues in Iran">Environmental issues in Iran</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Iran_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Iran_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/220px-Iran_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Iran_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/330px-Iran_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Iran_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/440px-Iran_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="500"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Iran_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> Climate map of Iran (
        <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen-Geiger" title="Köppen-Geiger" class="mw-redirect">Köppen-Geiger</a>) 
        <table style="width:100%;"> 
         <tbody>
          <tr> 
           <td valign="top">

             <a href="/wiki/Hot_desert_climate" title="Hot desert climate" class="mw-redirect">Hot desert climate</a>
            </div>

             <a href="/wiki/Cold_desert_climate" title="Cold desert climate" class="mw-redirect">Cold desert climate</a>
            </div>

             <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #F5A301; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;

         </tbody>
        </table> 
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Iran's <a href="/wiki/Climate" title="Climate">climate</a> ranges from <a href="/wiki/Desert_climate" title="Desert climate">arid</a> or <a href="/wiki/Semiarid" title="Semiarid" class="mw-redirect">semiarid</a>, to <a href="/wiki/Subtropical" title="Subtropical" class="mw-redirect">subtropical</a> along the Caspian coast and the <a href="/wiki/Jungles_of_Iran" title="Jungles of Iran" class="mw-redirect">northern forests</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-HaftlangLang2003_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HaftlangLang2003-156">[155]</a></sup> On the northern edge of the country (the Caspian coastal plain) temperatures rarely fall below freezing and the area remains humid for the rest of the year. Summer temperatures rarely exceed 29&nbsp;°C (84.2&nbsp;°F).<sup id="cite_ref-Nagarajan2010_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nagarajan2010-157">[156]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[157]</a></sup> Annual precipitation is 680&nbsp;mm (26.8&nbsp;in) in the eastern part of the plain and more than 1,700&nbsp;mm (66.9&nbsp;in) in the western part. United Nations Resident Coordinator for Iran Gary Lewis has said that "Water scarcity poses the most severe human security challenge in Iran today".<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[158]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>To the west, settlements in the <a href="/wiki/Zagros_Mountains" title="Zagros Mountains">Zagros</a> basin experience lower temperatures, severe winters with below zero average daily temperatures and heavy snowfall. The eastern and central basins are arid, with less than 200&nbsp;mm (7.9&nbsp;in) of rain, and have occasional deserts.<sup id="cite_ref-Nicholson2011_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nicholson2011-160">[159]</a></sup> Average summer temperatures rarely exceed 38&nbsp;°C (100.4&nbsp;°F).<sup id="cite_ref-Nagarajan2010_157-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nagarajan2010-157">[156]</a></sup> The coastal plains of the Persian Gulf and <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Oman" title="Gulf of Oman">Gulf of Oman</a> in southern Iran have mild winters, and very humid and hot summers. The annual precipitation ranges from 135 to 355&nbsp;mm (5.3 to 14.0&nbsp;in).<sup id="cite_ref-Nagarajan2010_157-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nagarajan2010-157">[156]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fauna">Fauna</span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote">
      See also: 
      <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_Iran" title="Wildlife of Iran">Wildlife of Iran</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Persian_Leopard_sitting.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Persian_Leopard_sitting.jpg/220px-Persian_Leopard_sitting.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Persian_Leopard_sitting.jpg/330px-Persian_Leopard_sitting.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Persian_Leopard_sitting.jpg/440px-Persian_Leopard_sitting.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Persian_Leopard_sitting.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Persian_leopard" title="Persian leopard">Persian leopard</a>, an 
        <a href="/wiki/Endangered_species" title="Endangered species">endangered species</a> living primarily in Iran
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The wildlife of Iran is composed of several animal species, including <a href="/wiki/Bears" title="Bears" class="mw-redirect">bears</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gazelles" title="Gazelles" class="mw-redirect">gazelles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wild_pigs" title="Wild pigs" class="mw-redirect">wild pigs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wolves" title="Wolves" class="mw-redirect">wolves</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jackals" title="Jackals" class="mw-redirect">jackals</a>, <a href="/wiki/Panthera" title="Panthera">panthers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_lynx" title="Eurasian lynx">Eurasian lynx</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Foxes" title="Foxes" class="mw-redirect">foxes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Fast2005_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fast2005-161">[160]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Firouz2005_162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Firouz2005-162">[161]</a></sup> The domestic animals of Iran include <a href="/wiki/Sheep" title="Sheep">sheep</a>, <a href="/wiki/Goats" title="Goats" class="mw-redirect">goats</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cattle" title="Cattle">cattle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Horses" title="Horses" class="mw-redirect">horses</a>, <a href="/wiki/Water_buffaloes" title="Water buffaloes" class="mw-redirect">water buffaloes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Donkeys" title="Donkeys" class="mw-redirect">donkeys</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Camels" title="Camels" class="mw-redirect">camels</a>. <a href="/wiki/Pheasant" title="Pheasant">Pheasants</a>, <a href="/wiki/Partridge" title="Partridge">partridges</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stork" title="Stork">storks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eagles" title="Eagles" class="mw-redirect">eagles</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Falcons" title="Falcons" class="mw-redirect">falcons</a> are also native to the wildlife of Iran.</p> 
     <p>One of the most famous members of the Iranian wildlife is the critically endangered <a href="/wiki/Asiatic_cheetah" title="Asiatic cheetah">Asiatic cheetah</a>, also known as the <i>Iranian cheetah</i>, whose numbers were greatly reduced after the 1979 Revolution.<sup id="cite_ref-Borrini-FeyerabendFarvar2013_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Borrini-FeyerabendFarvar2013-163">[162]</a></sup> Iran had lost all its <a href="/wiki/Asiatic_lion" title="Asiatic lion">Asiatic lions</a> and the now extinct <a href="/wiki/Caspian_tiger" title="Caspian tiger">Caspian tigers</a> by the earlier part of the 20th century.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">[163]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>At least 74 species of Iranian wildlife are on the red list of the <a href="/wiki/International_Union_for_the_Conservation_of_Nature" title="International Union for the Conservation of Nature" class="mw-redirect">International Union for the Conservation of Nature</a>, a sign of serious threats against the country’s biodiversity. The <a href="/wiki/Iranian_Parliament" title="Iranian Parliament" class="mw-redirect">Iranian Parliament</a> has been showing disregard for wildlife by passing laws and regulations such as the act that lets the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Industries_and_Mines_(Iran)" title="Ministry of Industries and Mines (Iran)">Ministry of Industries and Mines</a> exploit mines without the involvement of the <a href="/wiki/Department_of_Environment_(Iran)" title="Department of Environment (Iran)">Department of Environment</a>, and by approving large national development projects without demanding comprehensive study of their impact on wildlife habitats.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">[164]</a></sup></p> 
     <p><span id="Provinces_and_cities"></span><span id="Regions.2C_provinces_and_cities"></span><span id="Subdivisions"></span><span id="Administrative_divisions"></span></p>

       <a href="/wiki/File:The_most_populated_cities_of_iran.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/The_most_populated_cities_of_iran.svg/220px-The_most_populated_cities_of_iran.svg.png" width="220" height="196" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/The_most_populated_cities_of_iran.svg/330px-The_most_populated_cities_of_iran.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/The_most_populated_cities_of_iran.svg/440px-The_most_populated_cities_of_iran.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="800"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:The_most_populated_cities_of_iran.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> The most populated cities of Iran in 2010
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Iran is divided into five <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_Iran" title="Regions of Iran">regions</a> with thirty one <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Iran" title="Provinces of Iran">provinces</a> (<i>ostān</i>),<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">[165]</a></sup> each governed by an appointed governor (<i>ostāndār</i>). The provinces are divided into counties (<i><a href="/wiki/Counties_of_Iran" title="Counties of Iran">shahrestān</a></i>), and subdivided into districts (<i><a href="/wiki/Bakhsh" title="Bakhsh">bakhsh</a></i>) and sub-districts (<i>dehestān</i>).</p> 
     <p>Iran has one of the highest urban growth rates in the world. From 1950 to 2002, the urban proportion of the population increased from 27% to 60%.<sup id="cite_ref-payvand2_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-payvand2-167">[166]</a></sup> The United Nations predicts that by 2030, 80% of the population will be urban.<sup id="cite_ref-sci.org.ir_168-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sci.org.ir-168">[167]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (June 2013)">not in citation given</span></a></i>]</sup> Most internal migrants have settled near the cities of <a href="/wiki/Tehran" title="Tehran">Tehran</a>, <a href="/wiki/Isfahan" title="Isfahan">Isfahan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ahvaz" title="Ahvaz">Ahvaz</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Qom" title="Qom">Qom</a>. The listed populations are from the 2006/07 (1385&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Iranian_calendars" title="Iranian calendars">AP</a>) census.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">[168]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (June 2013)">not in citation given</span></a></i>]</sup></p> 
     <p>Tehran, with a population of around 8.1 million (2011 census), is the capital and largest city in Iran. It is an economical and cultural center in Iran, and is the hub of the country's <a href="/wiki/Communications_in_Iran" title="Communications in Iran">communication</a> and <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Iran" title="Transport in Iran">transport</a> network.</p> 
     <p>The country's second largest city, <a href="/wiki/Mashhad" title="Mashhad">Mashhad</a>, has a population of around 2.7 million (2011 census). It is the capital of <a href="/wiki/Razavi_Khorasan_Province" title="Razavi Khorasan Province">Razavi Khorasan Province</a>, and is a holy city in <a href="/wiki/Shia_Islam" title="Shia Islam">Shia Islam</a>, as it is the site of the <a href="/wiki/Imam_Reza_Shrine" title="Imam Reza Shrine" class="mw-redirect">Imam Reza Shrine</a>. About 15 to 20 million pilgrims visit the Shrine of Imam Reza every year.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">[169]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">[170]</a></sup></p> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Isfahan" title="Isfahan">Isfahan</a>, with a population of around 1.7 million (2011 census), is Iran's third largest city and the capital of <a href="/wiki/Isfahan_Province" title="Isfahan Province">Isfahan Province</a>. It was also a former capital of Iran, and contains a wide variety of historical sites; including the famous <a href="/wiki/Naqsh-e_Jahan_Square" title="Naqsh-e Jahan Square">Image of the World Square</a>, <a href="/wiki/Siose_Bridge" title="Siose Bridge" class="mw-redirect">Siose Bridge</a>, and the sites at the Armenian district of <a href="/wiki/New_Jolfa" title="New Jolfa" class="mw-redirect">New Jolfa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Iranicaonline.org_November_29_2015c_172-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Iranicaonline.org_November_29_2015c-172">[171]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>The fourth major city of Iran, <a href="/wiki/Karaj" title="Karaj">Karaj</a>, has a population of around 1.6 million (2011 census). It is the capital of <a href="/wiki/Alborz_Province" title="Alborz Province">Alborz Province</a>, and is situated 20&nbsp;km west of Tehran, at the foot of the <a href="/wiki/Alborz" title="Alborz">Alborz</a> mountains. It is a major industrial city in Iran, with large factories producing sugar, textiles, wire, and alcohol.</p> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Tabriz" title="Tabriz">Tabriz</a>, the capital of <a href="/wiki/East_Azerbaijan_Province" title="East Azerbaijan Province">East Azerbaijan Province</a>, is considered the second industrial city of Iran (after Tehran). With a population of around 1.4 million (2011 census), it is the fifth major city of Iran, which had been the second-largest until the late 1960s. It is one of the former capitals of Iran, the first capital of the <a href="/wiki/Safavid_Empire" title="Safavid Empire" class="mw-redirect">Safavid Empire</a>, and has also been proven extremely influential in the country’s recent history.</p> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Shiraz" title="Shiraz">Shiraz</a>, with a population of around 1.4 million (2011 census), is the sixth major city of Iran. It is the capital of <a href="/wiki/Fars_Province" title="Fars Province">Fars Province</a>, and was also a former capital of Iran. The area was greatly influenced by the <a href="/wiki/First_Babylonian_Dynasty" title="First Babylonian Dynasty">Babylonian</a> civilization, and after the emergence of the ancient <a href="/wiki/Persian_people" title="Persian people">Persians</a>, soon came to be known as <a href="/wiki/Persis" title="Persis">Persis</a>. Persians were present in the region since the 9th century BC, and became rulers of a large empire under the reign of the <a href="/wiki/Achaemenid_Dynasty" title="Achaemenid Dynasty" class="mw-redirect">Achaemenid Dynasty</a> in the 6th century BC. The ruins of <a href="/wiki/Persepolis" title="Persepolis">Persepolis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pasargadae" title="Pasargadae">Pasargadae</a>, two of the four capitals of the Achaemenid Empire, are located around the modern-day city of Shiraz.</p> 
     <p><br></p>
