     <div style="clear:both;"></div> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span></h2> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Iran" title="Politics of Iran">Politics of Iran</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Ali_Khamenei_and_Vladimir_Putin.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Ali_Khamenei_and_Vladimir_Putin.jpg/220px-Ali_Khamenei_and_Vladimir_Putin.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Ali_Khamenei_and_Vladimir_Putin.jpg/330px-Ali_Khamenei_and_Vladimir_Putin.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Ali_Khamenei_and_Vladimir_Putin.jpg/440px-Ali_Khamenei_and_Vladimir_Putin.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="682"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Ali_Khamenei_and_Vladimir_Putin.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Ali_Khamenei" title="Ali Khamenei">Ali Khamenei</a>, the Supreme Leader of Iran, meeting with Russian President 
        <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Vladimir Putin</a> on November 23, 2015
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Iran_gov_power_structure.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Iran_gov_power_structure.svg/220px-Iran_gov_power_structure.svg.png" width="220" height="115" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Iran_gov_power_structure.svg/330px-Iran_gov_power_structure.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Iran_gov_power_structure.svg/440px-Iran_gov_power_structure.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="996" data-file-height="522"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Iran_gov_power_structure.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> Iran's syncretic political system combines elements of a modern Islamic theocracy with democracy.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The political system of the Islamic Republic is based on the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_the_Islamic_Republic_of_Iran" title="Constitution of the Islamic Republic of Iran">1979 Constitution</a>, and comprises several intricately connected governing bodies. <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Leader_of_Iran" title="Supreme Leader of Iran">The Leader of the Revolution</a> ("Supreme Leader") is responsible for <a href="/wiki/Guardianship_of_the_Islamic_Jurists" title="Guardianship of the Islamic Jurists">delineation and supervision</a> of the general policies of the Islamic Republic of Iran.<sup id="cite_ref-leader_175-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-leader-175">[174]</a></sup> The Supreme Leader is Commander-in-Chief of the armed forces, controls the military intelligence and security operations, and has sole power to declare war or peace.<sup id="cite_ref-leader_175-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-leader-175">[174]</a></sup> The heads of the judiciary, state radio and television networks, the commanders of the police and military forces and six of the twelve members of the <a href="/wiki/Guardian_Council" title="Guardian Council">Guardian Council</a> are appointed by the Supreme Leader.<sup id="cite_ref-leader_175-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-leader-175">[174]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Assembly_of_Experts" title="Assembly of Experts">Assembly of Experts</a> elects and dismisses the Supreme Leader on the basis of qualifications and popular esteem.<sup id="cite_ref-loc_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-loc-176">[175]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>After the Supreme Leader, the Constitution defines the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Iran" title="President of Iran">President of Iran</a> as the highest state authority.<sup id="cite_ref-leader_175-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-leader-175">[174]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-photius_177-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-photius-177">[176]</a></sup> The President is elected by <a href="/wiki/Universal_suffrage" title="Universal suffrage">universal suffrage</a> for a term of four years and can only be re-elected for one term.<sup id="cite_ref-photius_177-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-photius-177">[176]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Disputed_statement" title="Wikipedia:Disputed statement" class="mw-redirect"><span title="The material near this tag is possibly inaccurate or nonfactual. (May 2012)">dubious</span></a> <span class="metadata">– <a href="/wiki/Talk:Iran#Presidential_Term_Limits" title="Talk:Iran">discuss</a></span></i>]</sup> Presidential candidates must be approved by the Guardian Council before running, in order to ensure their allegiance to the ideals of the Islamic Revolution.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">[177]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>The President is responsible for the implementation of the Constitution and for the exercise of executive powers, except for matters directly related to the Supreme Leader, who has the final say in all matters.<sup id="cite_ref-leader_175-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-leader-175">[174]</a></sup> The President appoints and supervises the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Minsters_of_Iran" title="Council of Minsters of Iran" class="mw-redirect">Council of Ministers</a>, coordinates government decisions, and selects government policies to be placed before the legislature.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">[178]</a></sup> Eight Vice-Presidents serve under the President, as well as a cabinet of twenty-two ministers, who must all be approved by the legislature.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">[179]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>The legislature of Iran (known as the <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Consultative_Assembly_(Iran)" title="Islamic Consultative Assembly (Iran)" class="mw-redirect">Islamic Consultative Assembly</a>) is a <a href="/wiki/Unicameral" title="Unicameral" class="mw-redirect">unicameral</a> body.<sup id="cite_ref-Majlis_181-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Majlis-181">[180]</a></sup> The Parliament of Iran comprises 290 members elected for four-year terms.<sup id="cite_ref-Majlis_181-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Majlis-181">[180]</a></sup> The parliament drafts legislation, ratifies international <a href="/wiki/Treaties" title="Treaties" class="mw-redirect">treaties</a>, and approves the national budget. All parliament candidates and all legislation from the assembly must be approved by the Guardian Council.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">[181]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>The Guardian Council comprises twelve jurists including six appointed by the Supreme Leader. The others are elected by the <a href="/wiki/Iranian_Parliament" title="Iranian Parliament" class="mw-redirect">Iranian Parliament</a> from among the jurists nominated by the Head of the <a href="/wiki/Judicial_system_of_Iran" title="Judicial system of Iran">Judiciary</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated4_183-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated4-183">[182]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">[183]</a></sup> The Council interprets the constitution and may veto Parliament. If a law is deemed incompatible with the constitution or <a href="/wiki/Sharia" title="Sharia">Sharia</a> (Islamic law), it is referred back to Parliament for revision.<sup id="cite_ref-photius_177-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-photius-177">[176]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Expediency_Discernment_Council" title="Expediency Discernment Council">Expediency Council</a> has the authority to mediate disputes between Parliament and the Guardian Council, and serves as an advisory body to the Supreme Leader, making it one of the most powerful governing bodies in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">[184]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/City_and_Village_Councils_of_Iran" title="City and Village Councils of Iran">Local city councils</a> are elected by public vote to four-year terms in all cities and villages of Iran.</p> 
     <p>Iran has adopted the <a href="/wiki/Separation_of_powers" title="Separation of powers">separation of powers</a>, having three typical division of branches: <a href="/wiki/President_of_Iran" title="President of Iran">Executive</a> (incumbent: <a href="/wiki/Hassan_Rouhani" title="Hassan Rouhani">Hassan Rouhani</a>), <a href="/wiki/List_of_Speakers_of_the_Parliament_of_Iran" title="List of Speakers of the Parliament of Iran">Legislature</a> (incumbent: <a href="/wiki/Ali_Larijani" title="Ali Larijani">Ali Larijani</a>), and the <a href="/wiki/Chief_Justice_of_Iran" title="Chief Justice of Iran">Judiciary</a> (incumbent: <a href="/wiki/Sadeq_Larijani" title="Sadeq Larijani">Sadeq Larijani</a>).</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Law">Law</span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles: 
      <a href="/wiki/Judicial_system_of_Iran" title="Judicial system of Iran">Judicial system of Iran</a> and 
      <a href="/wiki/Media_of_Iran" title="Media of Iran">Media of Iran</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Parliament_of_Iran_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/5a/Parliament_of_Iran_2.jpg/220px-Parliament_of_Iran_2.jpg" width="220" height="109" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/5a/Parliament_of_Iran_2.jpg/330px-Parliament_of_Iran_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/5a/Parliament_of_Iran_2.jpg/440px-Parliament_of_Iran_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1012"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Parliament_of_Iran_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> The 
        <a href="/wiki/Iranian_Parliament" title="Iranian Parliament" class="mw-redirect">Iranian Parliament</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The Supreme Leader appoints the head of Iran's judiciary, who in turn appoints the head of the Supreme Court and the chief public prosecutor.<sup id="cite_ref-Judiciary_186-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Judiciary-186">[185]</a></sup> There are several types of courts including public courts that deal with civil and criminal cases, and <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Revolutionary_Court" title="Islamic Revolutionary Court">revolutionary courts</a> which deal with certain categories of offenses, including crimes against <a href="/wiki/National_security" title="National security">national security</a>. The decisions of the revolutionary courts are final and cannot be appealed.<sup id="cite_ref-Judiciary_186-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Judiciary-186">[185]</a></sup> The Special Clerical Court handles crimes allegedly committed by <a href="/wiki/Cleric" title="Cleric" class="mw-redirect">clerics</a>, although it has also taken on cases involving <a href="/wiki/Layperson" title="Layperson">lay people</a>. The Special Clerical Court functions independently of the regular judicial framework and is accountable only to the Supreme Leader. The Court's rulings are final and cannot be appealed.<sup id="cite_ref-Judiciary_186-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Judiciary-186">[185]</a></sup> The Assembly of Experts, which meets for one week annually, comprises 86 "virtuous and learned" clerics elected by adult suffrage for eight-year terms. As with the presidential and parliamentary elections, the Guardian Council determines candidates' eligibility.<sup id="cite_ref-Judiciary_186-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Judiciary-186">[185]</a></sup> The Assembly elects the Supreme Leader and has the constitutional authority to remove the Supreme Leader from power at any time.<sup id="cite_ref-Judiciary_186-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Judiciary-186">[185]</a></sup> It has not challenged any of the Supreme Leader's decisions.<sup id="cite_ref-Judiciary_186-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Judiciary-186">[185]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>The state-owned <a href="/wiki/Telecommunication_Company_of_Iran" title="Telecommunication Company of Iran">Telecommunication Company of Iran</a> handles telecommunications. The <a href="/wiki/Media_of_Iran" title="Media of Iran">media of Iran</a> is a mixture of private and state-owned, but books and movies must be approved by the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Culture_and_Islamic_Guidance" title="Ministry of Culture and Islamic Guidance" class="mw-redirect">The ministry of Ershaad</a> before being released to the public. Iran originally received access to the internet in 1993, and it has become enormously popular among the Iranian youth.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Iran" title="Foreign relations of Iran">Foreign relations of Iran</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Hassan_Rouhani_and_Vladimir_Putin_(1).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Hassan_Rouhani_and_Vladimir_Putin_%281%29.jpg/220px-Hassan_Rouhani_and_Vladimir_Putin_%281%29.jpg" width="220" height="143" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Hassan_Rouhani_and_Vladimir_Putin_%281%29.jpg/330px-Hassan_Rouhani_and_Vladimir_Putin_%281%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Hassan_Rouhani_and_Vladimir_Putin_%281%29.jpg/440px-Hassan_Rouhani_and_Vladimir_Putin_%281%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="780"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Hassan_Rouhani_and_Vladimir_Putin_(1).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> Iranian President 
        <a href="/wiki/Hassan_Rouhani" title="Hassan Rouhani">Hassan Rouhani</a> meeting with Russian President 
        <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Vladimir Putin</a> – Iran and Russia are strategic allies.
        <sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">[186]</a></sup>
        <sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">[187]</a></sup>
        <sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">[188]</a></sup>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Secretary_Kerry_greets_Iranian_Foreign_Minister_Zarif.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Secretary_Kerry_greets_Iranian_Foreign_Minister_Zarif.jpg/220px-Secretary_Kerry_greets_Iranian_Foreign_Minister_Zarif.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Secretary_Kerry_greets_Iranian_Foreign_Minister_Zarif.jpg/330px-Secretary_Kerry_greets_Iranian_Foreign_Minister_Zarif.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Secretary_Kerry_greets_Iranian_Foreign_Minister_Zarif.jpg/440px-Secretary_Kerry_greets_Iranian_Foreign_Minister_Zarif.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2347" data-file-height="1557"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Secretary_Kerry_greets_Iranian_Foreign_Minister_Zarif.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> Iranian FM 
        <a href="/wiki/M._Javad_Zarif" title="M. Javad Zarif" class="mw-redirect">M. Javad Zarif</a> shaking hands with the US Secretary of State 
        <a href="/wiki/John_Kerry" title="John Kerry">John Kerry</a> during the 
        <a href="/wiki/Negotiations_leading_to_the_Joint_Comprehensive_Plan_of_Action" title="Negotiations leading to the Joint Comprehensive Plan of Action">Iranian nuclear talks</a> – There is no formal diplomatic relationship between Iran and the 
        <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">US</a>.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The Iranian government's officially stated goal is to establish a <a href="/wiki/New_world_order_(politics)" title="New world order (politics)">new world order</a> based on <a href="/wiki/World_peace" title="World peace">world peace</a>, global <a href="/wiki/Collective_security" title="Collective security">collective security</a> and justice.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">[189]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">[190]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Often, Iran's foreign relations since the time of the revolution have been portrayed as being based on two strategic principles: eliminating outside influences in the region and pursuing extensive diplomatic contacts with developing and <a href="/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement" title="Non-Aligned Movement">non-aligned countries</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">[191]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Since 2005, <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_program_of_Iran" title="Nuclear program of Iran">Iran's nuclear program</a> has become the subject of contention with the international community following earlier quotes of Iranian leadership favoring the use of an atomic bomb against Iran's enemies and in particular Israel.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">[192]</a></sup> Many countries have expressed concern that <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_program_of_Iran" title="Nuclear program of Iran">Iran's nuclear program</a> could divert civilian nuclear technology into a weapons program. This has led the <a href="/wiki/UN_Security_Council" title="UN Security Council" class="mw-redirect">UN Security Council</a> to impose <a href="/wiki/Sanctions_against_Iran" title="Sanctions against Iran">sanctions against Iran</a> which had further isolated Iran politically and economically from the rest of the global community. In 2009, the US <a href="/wiki/Director_of_National_Intelligence" title="Director of National Intelligence">Director of National Intelligence</a> said that Iran, if choosing to, would not be able to develop a nuclear weapon until 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">[193]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>As of 2009<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Iran&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Iran maintains diplomatic relations with 99 members of the United Nations,<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">[194]</a></sup> but not with the United States or Israel, a state which Iran has not recognized since the 1979 Revolution.<sup id="cite_ref-MousavianShahidsaless2014_196-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MousavianShahidsaless2014-196">[195]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>On July 14, 2015, Tehran and the <a href="/wiki/P5%2B1" title="P5+1">P5+1</a> came to a historic <a href="/wiki/Joint_Comprehensive_Plan_of_Action" title="Joint Comprehensive Plan of Action">agreement</a> to end <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_1929" title="United Nations Security Council Resolution 1929">economic sanctions</a> after demonstrating a peaceful nuclear research project that meets <a href="/wiki/International_Atomic_Energy_Agency" title="International Atomic Energy Agency">International Atomic Energy Agency</a> standards.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">[196]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Iran is also a member of dozens of international organizations including the <a href="/wiki/Group_of_15" title="Group of 15">G-15</a>, <a href="/wiki/Group_of_24" title="Group of 24">G-24</a>, <a href="/wiki/Group_of_77" title="Group of 77">G-77</a>, <a href="/wiki/IAEA" title="IAEA" class="mw-redirect">IAEA</a>, <a href="/wiki/IBRD" title="IBRD" class="mw-redirect">IBRD</a>, <a href="/wiki/International_Development_Association" title="International Development Association">IDA</a>, <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Development_Bank" title="Islamic Development Bank">IDB</a>, <a href="/wiki/International_Finance_Corporation" title="International Finance Corporation">IFC</a>, <a href="/wiki/International_Labour_Organization" title="International Labour Organization">ILO</a>, <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">IMF</a>, <a href="/wiki/International_Maritime_Organization" title="International Maritime Organization">International Maritime Organization</a>, <a href="/wiki/Interpol_(organization)" title="Interpol (organization)" class="mw-redirect">Interpol</a>, <a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_Islamic_Cooperation" title="Organisation of Islamic Cooperation">OIC</a>, <a href="/wiki/OPEC" title="OPEC">OPEC</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-rubin80_198-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rubin80-198">[197]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">WHO</a>, and currently has observer status at the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">World Trade Organization</a>.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles: 
      <a href="/wiki/Armed_Forces_of_the_Islamic_Republic_of_Iran" title="Armed Forces of the Islamic Republic of Iran">Armed Forces of the Islamic Republic of Iran</a> and 
      <a href="/wiki/Defense_industry_of_Iran" title="Defense industry of Iran">Defense industry of Iran</a>
     </div> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote">
      See also: 
      <a href="/wiki/Military_history_of_Iran" title="Military history of Iran">Military history of Iran</a> and 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_military_equipment_manufactured_in_Iran" title="List of military equipment manufactured in Iran">List of military equipment manufactured in Iran</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Fotros_drone.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/18/Fotros_drone.jpg/220px-Fotros_drone.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/18/Fotros_drone.jpg/330px-Fotros_drone.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/18/Fotros_drone.jpg/440px-Fotros_drone.jpg 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="342"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Fotros_drone.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Fotros_(UCAV)" title="Fotros (UCAV)" class="mw-redirect">Fotros (UCAV)</a> is considered the largest in Iran's arsenal of unmanned aerial vehicles. Iran has made several indigenous 
        <a href="/wiki/UAV" title="UAV" class="mw-redirect">UAVs</a>.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The Islamic Republic of Iran has two types of armed forces: the regular forces <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Republic_of_Iran_Army" title="Islamic Republic of Iran Army">Islamic Republic of Iran Army</a>, <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Republic_of_Iran_Air_Force" title="Islamic Republic of Iran Air Force">Islamic Republic of Iran Air Force</a>, <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Republic_of_Iran_Navy" title="Islamic Republic of Iran Navy">Islamic Republic of Iran Navy</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Army_of_the_Guardians_of_the_Islamic_Revolution" title="Army of the Guardians of the Islamic Revolution">Revolutionary Guards</a>, totaling about 545,000 active troops. Iran also has around 350,000 Reserve Force totaling around 900,000 trained troops.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">[198]</a></sup> Iran has a paramilitary, volunteer militia force within the IRGC, called the <a href="/wiki/Basij" title="Basij">Basij</a>, which includes about 90,000 full-time, active-duty uniformed members. Up to 11 million men and women are members of the Basij who could potentially be called up for service; GlobalSecurity.org estimates Iran could mobilize "up to one million men". This would be among the largest troop mobilizations in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">[199]</a></sup> In 2007, Iran's military spending represented 2.6% of the GDP or $102 per capita, the lowest figure of the <a href="/wiki/Persian_Gulf" title="Persian Gulf">Persian Gulf</a> nations.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">[200]</a></sup> Iran's military doctrine is based on <a href="/wiki/Deterrence_theory" title="Deterrence theory">deterrence</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">[201]</a></sup> In 2014 arms spending the country spent $15 billion and was outspent by the states of the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Cooperation_Council" title="Gulf Cooperation Council">Gulf Cooperation Council</a> by a factor of 13.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">[202]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Iran supports the military activities of its allies in Syria, Iraq, and Lebanon (<a href="/wiki/Hezbollah" title="Hezbollah">Hezbollah</a>) with thousands of rockets and missiles.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">[203]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Since the 1979 Revolution, to overcome foreign embargoes, Iran has developed its own military industry, produced its own <a href="/wiki/Tanks" title="Tanks" class="mw-redirect">tanks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Armored_personnel_carriers" title="Armored personnel carriers" class="mw-redirect">armored personnel carriers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guided_missile" title="Guided missile" class="mw-redirect">guided missiles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Submarine" title="Submarine">submarines</a>, military vessels, <a href="/wiki/Iranian_destroyer_Jamaran" title="Iranian destroyer Jamaran" class="mw-redirect">guided missile destroyer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Radar" title="Radar">radar</a> systems, <a href="/wiki/Helicopters" title="Helicopters" class="mw-redirect">helicopters</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fighter_planes" title="Fighter planes" class="mw-redirect">fighter planes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-AskariMohseni2010_205-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AskariMohseni2010-205">[204]</a></sup> In recent years, official announcements have highlighted the development of weapons such as the <a href="/wiki/Hoot_(missile)" title="Hoot (missile)" class="mw-redirect">Hoot</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kowsar" title="Kowsar">Kowsar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zelzal" title="Zelzal">Zelzal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fateh-110" title="Fateh-110">Fateh-110</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shahab-3" title="Shahab-3">Shahab-3</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sejjil" title="Sejjil">Sejjil</a> missiles, and a variety of <a href="/wiki/Unmanned_aerial_vehicles" title="Unmanned aerial vehicles" class="mw-redirect">unmanned aerial vehicles</a> (UAVs).<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">[205]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Fajr-3_(MIRV)" title="Fajr-3 (MIRV)" class="mw-redirect">Fajr-3 (MIRV)</a> is currently Iran's most advanced <a href="/wiki/Ballistic_missile" title="Ballistic missile">ballistic missile</a>, it is a <a href="/wiki/Liquid_fuel" title="Liquid fuel">liquid fuel</a> missile with an undisclosed range which was developed and produced domestically.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Iran" title="Economy of Iran">Economy of Iran</a>
     </div> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote">
      See also: 
      <a href="/wiki/Iranian_subsidy_reform_plan" title="Iranian subsidy reform plan">Iranian subsidy reform plan</a>, 
      <a href="/wiki/Tehran_Stock_Exchange" title="Tehran Stock Exchange">Tehran Stock Exchange</a>, 
      <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Iran" title="Transport in Iran">Transport in Iran</a> and 
      <a href="/wiki/Communications_in_Iran" title="Communications in Iran">Communications in Iran</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:272px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Provinces_of_Iran_by_contribution_to_national_GDP.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Provinces_of_Iran_by_contribution_to_national_GDP.svg/270px-Provinces_of_Iran_by_contribution_to_national_GDP.svg.png" width="270" height="240" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Provinces_of_Iran_by_contribution_to_national_GDP.svg/405px-Provinces_of_Iran_by_contribution_to_national_GDP.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Provinces_of_Iran_by_contribution_to_national_GDP.svg/540px-Provinces_of_Iran_by_contribution_to_national_GDP.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="800"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Provinces_of_Iran_by_contribution_to_national_GDP.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Iran" title="Provinces of Iran">Provinces of Iran</a> by contribution to national GDP in 2014
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Iran" title="Economy of Iran">Iran's economy</a> is a <a href="/wiki/Mixed_economy" title="Mixed economy">mixture</a> of <a href="/wiki/Planned_economy" title="Planned economy">central planning</a>, <a href="/wiki/State_ownership" title="State ownership">state ownership</a> of oil and other large enterprises, village agriculture, and small-scale private trading and service ventures.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">[206]</a></sup> In 2014, GDP was $404.1 billion ($1.334 trillion at PPP), or $17,100 at <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">PPP</a> per capita.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_34-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-34">[34]</a></sup> Iran is ranked as an upper-middle income economy by the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">[207]</a></sup> In the early 21st century the service sector contributed the largest percentage of the GDP, followed by industry (<a href="/wiki/Mining_in_Iran" title="Mining in Iran">mining</a> and manufacturing) and <a href="/wiki/Agriculture_of_Iran" title="Agriculture of Iran" class="mw-redirect">agriculture</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">[208]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Central_Bank_of_the_Islamic_Republic_of_Iran" title="Central Bank of the Islamic Republic of Iran">Central Bank of the Islamic Republic of Iran</a> is responsible for developing and maintaining the <a href="/wiki/Iranian_rial" title="Iranian rial">Iranian rial</a>, which serves as the country's <a href="/wiki/Currency" title="Currency">currency</a>. The government doesn't recognize <a href="/wiki/List_of_trade_unions#Iran" title="List of trade unions">trade unions</a> other than the <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Labour_Council" title="Islamic Labour Council" class="mw-redirect">Islamic Labour Councils</a>, which are subject to the approval of employers and the security services.<sup id="cite_ref-ayatoil_210-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ayatoil-210">[209]</a></sup> The minimum wage in June 2013 was 487 million rials a month ($134).<sup id="cite_ref-irannum_211-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-irannum-211">[210]</a></sup> Unemployment has remained above 10% since 1997, and the unemployment rate for women is almost double that of the men.<sup id="cite_ref-irannum_211-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-irannum-211">[210]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>In 2006, about 45% of the government's budget came from oil and natural gas revenues, and 31% came from taxes and fees.<sup id="cite_ref-payvand.com_212-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-payvand.com-212">[211]</a></sup> As of 2007<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Iran&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Iran had earned $70 billion in <a href="/wiki/Foreign_exchange_reserves" title="Foreign exchange reserves" class="mw-redirect">foreign exchange reserves</a> mostly (80%) from crude oil exports.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">[212]</a></sup> Iranian budget <a href="/wiki/Deficits" title="Deficits" class="mw-redirect">deficits</a> have been a chronic problem, mostly due to <a href="/wiki/Iranian_Economic_Reform_Plan#Subsidy_reform_plan" title="Iranian Economic Reform Plan" class="mw-redirect">large-scale state subsidies</a>, that include foodstuffs and especially gasoline, totaling more than $84 billion in 2008 for the energy sector alone.<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">[213]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">[214]</a></sup> In 2010, the <a href="/wiki/Iranian_Economic_Reform_Plan#Subsidy_reform_plan" title="Iranian Economic Reform Plan" class="mw-redirect">economic reform plan</a> was approved by parliament to <a href="/wiki/Iranian_subsidy_reform_plan" title="Iranian subsidy reform plan">cut subsidies</a> gradually and replace them with targeted social assistance. The objective is to move towards <a href="/wiki/Free_market" title="Free market">free market</a> prices in a 5-year period and increase productivity and <a href="/wiki/Social_justice" title="Social justice">social justice</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">[215]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>The administration continues to follow the <a href="/wiki/Iranian_Economic_Reform_Plan" title="Iranian Economic Reform Plan" class="mw-redirect">market reform plans</a> of the previous one and indicated that it will diversify Iran's oil-reliant economy. Iran has also developed a <a href="/wiki/Science_in_Iran#Biotechnology" title="Science in Iran" class="mw-redirect">biotechnology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Science_in_Iran#Nanotechnology" title="Science in Iran" class="mw-redirect">nanotechnology</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Pharmaceuticals_in_Iran" title="Pharmaceuticals in Iran" class="mw-redirect">pharmaceuticals</a> industry.<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">[216]</a></sup> However, nationalized industries such as the <a href="/wiki/Bonyad" title="Bonyad">bonyads</a> have often been managed badly, making them ineffective and uncompetitive with years. Currently, the government is trying to <a href="/wiki/Privatization_in_Iran" title="Privatization in Iran">privatize these industries</a>, and, despite successes, there are still several problems to be overcome, such as the <a href="/wiki/Corruption_in_Iran" title="Corruption in Iran">lagging corruption in the public sector</a> and lack of competitiveness. In 2010, Iran was ranked 69, out of 139 nations, in the <a href="/wiki/Global_Competitiveness_Report" title="Global Competitiveness Report">Global Competitiveness Report</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-WEF_218-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WEF-218">[217]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Iran has leading manufacturing industries in the fields of car-manufacture and transportation, construction materials, home appliances, food and agricultural goods, armaments, pharmaceuticals, information technology, power and petrochemicals in the Middle East.<sup id="cite_ref-Economy_219-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Economy-219">[218]</a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/Food_and_Agriculture_Organization" title="Food and Agriculture Organization">FAO</a>, Iran has been a top five producer of the following agricultural products in the world in 2012: <a href="/wiki/Apricot" title="Apricot">apricots</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cherry" title="Cherry">cherries</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sour_cherry" title="Sour cherry" class="mw-redirect">sour cherries</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cucumber" title="Cucumber">cucumbers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gherkin" title="Gherkin" class="mw-redirect">gherkins</a>, <a href="/wiki/Date_(fruit)" title="Date (fruit)" class="mw-redirect">dates</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eggplant" title="Eggplant">eggplants</a>, <a href="/wiki/Common_fig" title="Common fig">figs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pistachio" title="Pistachio">pistachios</a>, <a href="/wiki/Quince" title="Quince">quinces</a>, <a href="/wiki/Walnut" title="Walnut">walnuts</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Watermelon" title="Watermelon">watermelons</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">[219]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Economic <a href="/wiki/Sanctions_against_Iran" title="Sanctions against Iran">sanctions against Iran</a>, such as the embargo against Iranian crude oil, have affected the economy.<sup id="cite_ref-everend_221-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-everend-221">[220]</a></sup> Sanctions have led to a steep fall in the value of the rial, and as of April 2013 one US dollar is worth 36,000 rial, compared with 16,000 in early 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">[221]</a></sup> Following a successful implementation of the <a href="/wiki/Joint_Comprehensive_Plan_of_Action" title="Joint Comprehensive Plan of Action">2015 nuclear and sanctions relief deal</a>, the resulting benefits might not be distributed evenly across the Iranian economy as political elites such as the <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Revolutionary_Guard_Corps" title="Islamic Revolutionary Guard Corps" class="mw-redirect">Islamic Revolutionary Guard Corps</a> have garnered more resources and economic interests.<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">[222]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">[223]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Iran" title="Tourism in Iran">Tourism in Iran</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Kish-island-Persian-Gulf.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Kish-island-Persian-Gulf.jpg/220px-Kish-island-Persian-Gulf.jpg" width="220" height="116" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Kish-island-Persian-Gulf.jpg/330px-Kish-island-Persian-Gulf.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Kish-island-Persian-Gulf.jpg/440px-Kish-island-Persian-Gulf.jpg 2x" data-file-width="490" data-file-height="259"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Kish-island-Persian-Gulf.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> Over 1 million tourists visit 
        <a href="/wiki/Kish_Island" title="Kish Island">Kish Island</a> each year.
        <sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">[224]</a></sup>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Although tourism declined significantly during the war with Iraq, it has been subsequently recovered. About 1,659,000 foreign tourists visited Iran in 2004, and 2.3 million in 2009, mostly from Asian countries, including the republics of <a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">Central Asia</a>, while about 10% came from the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> and <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Encarta:_Iran.27s_entry_226-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encarta:_Iran.27s_entry-226">[225]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Tourism_227-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tourism-227">[226]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-presstvtour_228-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-presstvtour-228">[227]</a></sup> Over five million tourists visited Iran in the fiscal year of 2014–2015, ending March 21, four percent more year-on-year.<sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">[228]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Alongside the capital, the most popular tourist destinations are <a href="/wiki/Isfahan" title="Isfahan">Isfahan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mashhad" title="Mashhad">Mashhad</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shiraz" title="Shiraz">Shiraz</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">[229]</a></sup> In the early 2000s, the industry faced serious limitations in infrastructure, communications, industry standards and personnel training.<sup id="cite_ref-LOC7_231-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LOC7-231">[230]</a></sup> The majority of the 300,000 <a href="/wiki/Tourist_visa" title="Tourist visa" class="mw-redirect">tourist visas</a> granted in 2003 were obtained by Asian <a href="/wiki/Muslims" title="Muslims" class="mw-redirect">Muslims</a>, who presumably intended to visit important <a href="/wiki/Pilgrimage" title="Pilgrimage">pilgrimage</a> sites in <a href="/wiki/Mashhad" title="Mashhad">Mashhad</a> and <a href="/wiki/Qom" title="Qom">Qom</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-presstvtour_228-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-presstvtour-228">[227]</a></sup> Several organized tours from Germany, France and other European countries come to Iran annually to visit archaeological sites and monuments. In 2003, Iran ranked 68th in tourism revenues worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-IRNA5_232-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IRNA5-232">[231]</a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> and the deputy head of research for <a href="/wiki/Cultural_Heritage,_Handcrafts_and_Tourism_Organization" title="Cultural Heritage, Handcrafts and Tourism Organization">Iran Travel and Tourism Organization (ITTO)</a>, Iran is rated 4th among the top 10 destinations in the <a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">Middle East</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-IRNA5_232-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IRNA5-232">[231]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Domestic_tourism" title="Domestic tourism">Domestic tourism</a> in Iran is one of the largest in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-Tourism2_233-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tourism2-233">[232]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BYI_234-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BYI-234">[233]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MACooper2012_235-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MACooper2012-235">[234]</a></sup> Weak advertising, unstable regional conditions, a poor public image in some parts of the world, and absence of efficient planning schemes in the tourism sector have all hindered the growth of tourism.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy">Energy</span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles: 
      <a href="/wiki/Energy_in_Iran" title="Energy in Iran">Energy in Iran</a>, 
      <a href="/wiki/Petroleum_industry_in_Iran" title="Petroleum industry in Iran">Petroleum industry in Iran</a>, 
      <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_program_of_Iran" title="Nuclear program of Iran">Nuclear program of Iran</a> and 
      <a href="/wiki/Foreign_direct_investment_in_Iran" title="Foreign direct investment in Iran">Foreign direct investment in Iran</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:CIAIranKarteOelGas.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/CIAIranKarteOelGas.jpg/220px-CIAIranKarteOelGas.jpg" width="220" height="226" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/CIAIranKarteOelGas.jpg/330px-CIAIranKarteOelGas.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/CIAIranKarteOelGas.jpg/440px-CIAIranKarteOelGas.jpg 2x" data-file-width="687" data-file-height="705"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:CIAIranKarteOelGas.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> Iran holds 10% of the world's proven 
        <a href="/wiki/Oil_reserves" title="Oil reserves">oil reserves</a> and 15% of its gas. It is 
        <a href="/wiki/OPEC" title="OPEC">OPEC</a>'s second largest exporter and the world's fourth oil producer.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Iran has the second largest proved <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas_reserves_in_Iran" title="Natural gas reserves in Iran">gas reserves</a> in the world after <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>, with 33.6 trillion <a href="/wiki/Cubic_metres" title="Cubic metres" class="mw-redirect">cubic metres</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-wsjgas_236-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wsjgas-236">[235]</a></sup> and third <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_natural_gas_production" title="List of countries by natural gas production">largest natural gas production</a> in the world after <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>. It also ranks fourth in <a href="/wiki/Oil_reserves_in_Iran" title="Oil reserves in Iran">oil reserves</a> with an estimated 153,600,000,000 barrels.<sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">[236]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238">[237]</a></sup> It is <a href="/wiki/OPEC" title="OPEC">OPEC</a>'s 2nd largest oil exporter and is an <a href="/wiki/Energy_superpower#Iran" title="Energy superpower">energy superpower</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">[238]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-240" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240">[239]</a></sup> In 2005, Iran spent US$4 billion on fuel imports, because of <a href="/wiki/Smuggling_in_Iran" title="Smuggling in Iran" class="mw-redirect">contraband</a> and inefficient domestic use.<sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241">[240]</a></sup> Oil industry output averaged 4 million barrels per day (640,000&nbsp;m<sup>3</sup>/d) in 2005, compared with the peak of six million barrels per day reached in 1974. In the early years of the 2000s (decade), industry infrastructure was increasingly inefficient because of technological lags. Few exploratory <a href="/wiki/Oil_well" title="Oil well">wells</a> were drilled in 2005.</p> 
     <p>In 2004, a large share of <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas_reserves_in_Iran" title="Natural gas reserves in Iran">natural gas reserves in Iran</a> were untapped. The addition of new <a href="/wiki/Hydroelectric" title="Hydroelectric" class="mw-redirect">hydroelectric</a> stations and the streamlining of conventional coal and oil-fired stations increased installed capacity to 33,000 megawatts. Of that amount, about 75% was based on natural gas, 18% on oil, and 7% on hydroelectric power. In 2004, Iran opened its first wind-powered and geothermal plants, and the first <a href="/wiki/Solar_power" title="Solar power">solar</a> thermal plant is to come online in 2009. Iran is the third country in the world to have developed <a href="/wiki/Gas_to_liquid" title="Gas to liquid" class="mw-redirect">GTL</a> technology.<sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242">[241]</a></sup></p> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Iran" title="Demographics of Iran">Demographic</a> trends and intensified industrialization have caused <a href="/wiki/Electric_power" title="Electric power">electric power</a> demand to grow by 8% per year. The government’s goal of 53,000 megawatts of installed capacity by 2010 is to be reached by bringing on line <a href="/wiki/List_of_power_stations_in_Iran" title="List of power stations in Iran">new gas-fired plants</a> and by adding hydroelectric, and nuclear power generating capacity. <a href="/wiki/Bushehr_Nuclear_Power_Plant" title="Bushehr Nuclear Power Plant">Iran’s first nuclear power plant</a> at <a href="/wiki/Bushehr" title="Bushehr">Bushehr</a> went online in 2011. It is the second <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_Power_Plant" title="Nuclear Power Plant" class="mw-redirect">Nuclear Power Plant</a> that ever built in the Middle East after <a href="/wiki/Metsamor_Nuclear_Power_Plant" title="Metsamor Nuclear Power Plant">Metsamor Nuclear Power Plant</a> in <a href="/wiki/Armenia" title="Armenia">Armenia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-nuclear_243-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nuclear-243">[242]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-M.C3.BCllerM.C3.BCller2015_244-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-M.C3.BCllerM.C3.BCller2015-244">[243]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education.2C_science_and_technology">Education, science and technology</span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles: 
      <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Iran" title="Education in Iran">Education in Iran</a>, 
      <a href="/wiki/Higher_education_in_Iran" title="Higher education in Iran">Higher education in Iran</a> and 
      <a href="/wiki/Science_and_technology_in_Iran" title="Science and technology in Iran">Science and technology in Iran</a>
     </div> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote">
      See also: 
      <a href="/wiki/Venture_capital_in_Iran" title="Venture capital in Iran" class="mw-redirect">Venture capital in Iran</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Astrolabe-Persian-18C.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Astrolabe-Persian-18C.jpg/170px-Astrolabe-Persian-18C.jpg" width="170" height="156" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Astrolabe-Persian-18C.jpg/255px-Astrolabe-Persian-18C.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Astrolabe-Persian-18C.jpg/340px-Astrolabe-Persian-18C.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1061" data-file-height="972"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Astrolabe-Persian-18C.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> An 18th century Persian 
        <a href="/wiki/Astrolabe" title="Astrolabe">astrolabe</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Education_in_Iran" title="Education in Iran">Education in Iran</a> is highly centralized. <a href="/wiki/K-12_education" title="K-12 education" class="mw-redirect">K-12 education</a> is supervised by the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Education_(Iran)" title="Ministry of Education (Iran)">Ministry of Education</a>, and higher education is under the supervision of the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Science,_Research_and_Technology" title="Ministry of Science, Research and Technology" class="mw-redirect">Ministry of Science and Technology</a>. The adult literacy rated 93.0% in September 2015,<sup id="cite_ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245">[244]</a></sup> while it had rated 85.0% in 2008, up from 36.5% in 1976.<sup id="cite_ref-unescolit_246-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unescolit-246">[245]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>The requirement to enter into higher education is to have a <a href="/wiki/High_school_diploma" title="High school diploma">high school diploma</a> and pass the national university entrance examination, <a href="/wiki/Iranian_University_Entrance_Exam" title="Iranian University Entrance Exam">Iranian University Entrance Exam</a> (known as <i>concour</i>), which is the equivalent of the US <a href="/wiki/SAT" title="SAT">SAT</a> exams. Many students do a 1–2 year course of <a href="/wiki/University-preparatory_school" title="University-preparatory school">pre-university</a> (<i>piš-dānešgāh</i>), which is the equivalent of <a href="/wiki/General_Certificate_of_Education" title="General Certificate of Education">GCE</a> <a href="/wiki/A-levels" title="A-levels" class="mw-redirect">A-levels</a> and <a href="/wiki/International_Baccalaureate" title="International Baccalaureate">International Baccalaureate</a>. The completion of the pre-university course earns students the Pre-University Certificate.<sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247">[246]</a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:The_central_offices.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/The_central_offices.jpg/220px-The_central_offices.jpg" width="220" height="108" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/The_central_offices.jpg/330px-The_central_offices.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/The_central_offices.jpg/440px-The_central_offices.jpg 2x" data-file-width="524" data-file-height="257"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:The_central_offices.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> Central office of the 
        <a href="/wiki/Ferdowsi_University" title="Ferdowsi University" class="mw-redirect">FUM</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Higher education is sanctioned by different levels of diplomas. <i>Kārdāni</i> (<a href="/wiki/Associate_degree" title="Associate degree">associate degree</a>; also known as <i>fowq e diplom</i>) is delivered after 2 years of higher education; <i>kāršenāsi</i> (<a href="/wiki/Bachelor%27s_degree" title="Bachelor's degree">bachelor's degree</a>; also known as <i>licāns</i>) is delivered after 4 years of higher education; and <i>kāršenāsi e aršad</i> (<a href="/wiki/Master%27s_degree" title="Master's degree">master's degree</a>) is delivered after 2 more years of study, after which another exam allows the candidate to pursue a doctoral program (<a href="/wiki/PhD" title="PhD" class="mw-redirect">PhD</a>; known as <i>doctorā</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-wes.org_248-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wes.org-248">[247]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>According to the <a href="/wiki/Webometrics_Ranking_of_World_Universities" title="Webometrics Ranking of World Universities">Webometrics Ranking of World Universities</a>, the top-ranking universities in the country are the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Tehran" title="University of Tehran">University of Tehran</a> (468th worldwide), the <a href="/wiki/Tehran_University_of_Medical_Sciences" title="Tehran University of Medical Sciences">Tehran University of Medical Sciences</a> (612th) and <a href="/wiki/Ferdowsi_University_of_Mashhad" title="Ferdowsi University of Mashhad">Ferdowsi University of Mashhad</a> (815th).<sup id="cite_ref-249" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-249">[248]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Iran has increased its publication output nearly tenfold from 1996 through 2004, and has been ranked first in terms of output growth rate, followed by China.<sup id="cite_ref-250" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-250">[249]</a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/SCImago" title="SCImago" class="mw-redirect">SCImago</a>, Iran could rank fourth in the world in terms of research output by 2018, if the current trend persists.<sup id="cite_ref-Pakistanaffairs.pk_November_29_2015c_251-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pakistanaffairs.pk_November_29_2015c-251">[250]</a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Omid_0651.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Omid_0651.jpg/200px-Omid_0651.jpg" width="200" height="267" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Omid_0651.jpg/300px-Omid_0651.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Omid_0651.jpg/400px-Omid_0651.jpg 2x" data-file-width="450" data-file-height="600"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Omid_0651.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Safir_rocket" title="Safir rocket" class="mw-redirect">Safir rocket</a> – Iran is the 
        <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_first_orbital_launches_by_country#List_of_first_orbital_launches_by_country" title="Timeline of first orbital launches by country">ninth country to put a domestically built satellite into orbit</a> and the sixth to send 
        <a href="/wiki/Animals_in_space" title="Animals in space">animals in space</a>.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>In 2009, a SUSE Linux-based HPC system made by the Aerospace Research Institute of Iran (ARI) was launched with 32 cores, and now runs 96 cores. Its performance was pegged at 192 <a href="/wiki/GFLOPS" title="GFLOPS" class="mw-redirect">GFLOPS</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-252" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-252">[251]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Surena_(robot)" title="Surena (robot)">Sorena 2</a> Robot, which was designed by engineers at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Tehran" title="University of Tehran">University of Tehran</a>, was unveiled in 2010. The <a href="/wiki/Institute_of_Electrical_and_Electronics_Engineers" title="Institute of Electrical and Electronics Engineers">Institute of Electrical and Electronics Engineers</a> (IEEE) has placed the name of Surena among the five prominent robots of the world after analyzing its performance.<sup id="cite_ref-253" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-253">[252]</a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Inside_Aryogen.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/11/Inside_Aryogen.jpg/220px-Inside_Aryogen.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/11/Inside_Aryogen.jpg/330px-Inside_Aryogen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/11/Inside_Aryogen.jpg/440px-Inside_Aryogen.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="534"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Inside_Aryogen.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> Production line for 
        <a href="/wiki/AryoSeven" title="AryoSeven" class="mw-redirect">AryoSeven</a>, inside the biopharmaceutical company of 
        <a href="/wiki/AryoGen" title="AryoGen">AryoGen</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>In the biomedical sciences, Iran's <a href="/wiki/Institute_of_Biochemistry_and_Biophysics" title="Institute of Biochemistry and Biophysics">Institute of Biochemistry and Biophysics</a> is a UNESCO chair in biology.<sup id="cite_ref-254" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-254">[253]</a></sup> In late 2006, <a href="/wiki/List_of_modern_Iranian_scientists" title="List of modern Iranian scientists" class="mw-redirect">Iranian scientists</a> successfully <a href="/wiki/Cloning" title="Cloning">cloned</a> a sheep by somatic cell nuclear transfer, at the <a href="/wiki/Royan_Institute" title="Royan Institute">Royan Research Center</a> in Tehran.<sup id="cite_ref-255" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-255">[254]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>According to a study by David Morrison and Ali Khadem Hosseini (Harvard-MIT and Cambridge), <a href="/wiki/Stem_cell" title="Stem cell">stem cell</a> research in Iran is amongst the top 10 in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-256" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-256">[255]</a></sup> Iran ranks 15th in the world in <a href="/wiki/Nanotechnologies" title="Nanotechnologies" class="mw-redirect">nanotechnologies</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-257" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-257">[256]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-258" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-258">[257]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-259" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-259">[258]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Iran placed its domestically built <a href="/wiki/Satellite" title="Satellite">satellite</a>, <a href="/wiki/Omid" title="Omid">Omid</a> into orbit on the 30th anniversary of the 1979 Revolution, on 2 February 2009,<sup id="cite_ref-HarveySmid2011_260-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HarveySmid2011-260">[259]</a></sup> through <a href="/wiki/Safir_(rocket)" title="Safir (rocket)">Safir rocket</a>, becoming the <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_first_orbital_launches_by_country" title="Timeline of first orbital launches by country">ninth country</a> in the world capable of both producing a satellite and sending it into <a href="/wiki/Space" title="Space">space</a> from a domestically made <a href="/wiki/Launch_pad" title="Launch pad">launcher</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Hvac-conference.ir_November_29_2015c_261-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hvac-conference.ir_November_29_2015c-261">[260]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Iranian_nuclear_program" title="Iranian nuclear program" class="mw-redirect">Iranian nuclear program</a> was launched in the 1950s. Iran is the seventh country to produce <a href="/wiki/Uranium_hexafluoride" title="Uranium hexafluoride">uranium hexafluoride</a>, and controls the entire <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_fuel_cycle" title="Nuclear fuel cycle">nuclear fuel cycle</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-262" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-262">[261]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-263" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-263">[262]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Iranian scientists outside Iran have also made some major contributions to science. In 1960, <a href="/wiki/Ali_Javan" title="Ali Javan">Ali Javan</a> co-invented the first <a href="/wiki/Gas_laser" title="Gas laser">gas laser</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Fuzzy_set" title="Fuzzy set">fuzzy set theory</a> was introduced by <a href="/wiki/Lotfi_Zadeh" title="Lotfi Zadeh" class="mw-redirect">Lotfi Zadeh</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-264" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-264">[263]</a></sup> Iranian cardiologist, <a href="/wiki/Tofy_Mussivand" title="Tofy Mussivand">Tofy Mussivand</a> invented and developed the first artificial cardiac pump, the precursor of the <a href="/wiki/Artificial_heart" title="Artificial heart">artificial heart</a>. Furthering research and treatment of diabetes, <a href="/wiki/HbA1c" title="HbA1c" class="mw-redirect">HbA1c</a> was discovered by <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Rahbar" title="Samuel Rahbar">Samuel Rahbar</a>. Iranian physics is especially strong in <a href="/wiki/String_theory" title="String theory">string theory</a>, with many papers being published in Iran.<sup id="cite_ref-Nasr2007_265-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nasr2007-265">[264]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Iranian-American" title="Iranian-American" class="mw-redirect">Iranian-American</a> string theorist <a href="/wiki/Kamran_Vafa" title="Kamran Vafa" class="mw-redirect">Kamran Vafa</a> proposed the <a href="/wiki/Vafa-Witten_theorem" title="Vafa-Witten theorem" class="mw-redirect">Vafa-Witten theorem</a> together with <a href="/wiki/Edward_Witten" title="Edward Witten">Edward Witten</a>. In August 2014, <a href="/wiki/Maryam_Mirzakhani" title="Maryam Mirzakhani">Maryam Mirzakhani</a> became the first-ever woman, as well as the first-ever Iranian, to receive the <a href="/wiki/Fields_Medal" title="Fields Medal">Fields Medal</a>, the highest prize in mathematics.<sup id="cite_ref-266" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-266">[265]</a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:272px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Provinces_of_Iran_by_population.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Provinces_of_Iran_by_population.svg/270px-Provinces_of_Iran_by_population.svg.png" width="270" height="240" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Provinces_of_Iran_by_population.svg/405px-Provinces_of_Iran_by_population.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Provinces_of_Iran_by_population.svg/540px-Provinces_of_Iran_by_population.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="800"></a>

       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:272px;">
