     <p>Iran is a diverse country, consisting of many religious and ethnic groups that are unified through a shared <a href="/wiki/Persian_culture" title="Persian culture" class="mw-redirect">Persian language and culture</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-268" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-268">[267]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Iran's population grew rapidly during the latter half of the 20th century, increasing from about 19 million in 1956 to around 75 million by 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-una_269-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-una-269">[268]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-270" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-270">[269]</a></sup> However, Iran's <a href="/wiki/Birth_rate" title="Birth rate">birth rate</a> has dropped significantly in recent years, leading to a population growth rate—recorded from July 2012—of about 1.29%.<sup id="cite_ref-DW_Persian_271-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DW_Persian-271">[270]</a></sup> Studies project that the growth will continue to slow until it stabilizes above 105 million by 2050.<sup id="cite_ref-bureau_272-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bureau-272">[271]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-payvand_273-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-payvand-273">[272]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Iran hosts one of the largest <a href="/wiki/Refugee" title="Refugee">refugee</a> populations in the world, with more than one million refugees, mostly from <a href="/wiki/Afghan_refugees" title="Afghan refugees">Afghanistan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-274" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-274">[273]</a></sup> Since 2006, Iranian officials have been working with the <a href="/wiki/UNHCR" title="UNHCR" class="mw-redirect">UNHCR</a> and Afghan officials for their <a href="/wiki/Repatriation" title="Repatriation">repatriation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bbcb_275-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbcb-275">[274]</a></sup> According to estimates, about five million <a href="/wiki/Iranian_citizens_abroad" title="Iranian citizens abroad" class="mw-redirect">Iranian citizens</a> have emigrated to other countries, mostly since the 1979 Revolution.<sup id="cite_ref-Ganji2002_276-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ganji2002-276">[275]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-277" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-277">[276]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>According to the <a href="/wiki/Iranian_Constitution" title="Iranian Constitution" class="mw-redirect">Iranian Constitution</a>, the government is required to provide every citizen of the country with access to <a href="/wiki/Social_security" title="Social security">social security</a> that covers retirement, unemployment, old age, <a href="/wiki/Disability" title="Disability">disability</a>, accidents, calamities, health and medical treatment and care services.<sup id="cite_ref-278" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-278">[277]</a></sup> This is covered by <a href="/wiki/Labor_and_tax_laws_in_Iran" title="Labor and tax laws in Iran" class="mw-redirect">tax revenues</a> and income derived from public contributions.<sup id="cite_ref-279" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-279">[278]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Iran" title="Languages of Iran">Languages of Iran</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The majority of the population speak <a href="/wiki/Persian_language" title="Persian language">Persian language</a>, which is also the <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">official language</a> of the country. Others include speakers of the rest of the <a href="/wiki/Iranian_language" title="Iranian language" class="mw-redirect">Iranian languages</a> within the greater <a href="/wiki/Indo-European_languages" title="Indo-European languages">Indo-European languages</a>, and the languages of the other ethnicities in Iran.</p> 
     <p>In northern Iran, mostly confined to <a href="/wiki/Gilan_Province" title="Gilan Province">Gilan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mazandaran_Province" title="Mazandaran Province">Mazenderan</a> provinces, <a href="/wiki/Gilaki_language" title="Gilaki language">Gilaki</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mazandarani_language" title="Mazandarani language" class="mw-redirect">Mazenderani</a> languages are widely spoken, which are classified as either a dialect of Persian or a different Iranian language. They both have affinities to the neighboring <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_the_Caucasus" title="Languages of the Caucasus">Caucasian languages</a>. In parts of Gilan, <a href="/wiki/Talysh_language" title="Talysh language">Talysh language</a> is also widely spoken, which stretches up to the neighboring country of <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan" title="Azerbaijan">Azerbaijan</a>. <a href="/wiki/Kurdish_language" title="Kurdish language" class="mw-redirect">Kurdish</a> is widely spoken in <a href="/wiki/Kurdistan_Province" title="Kurdistan Province">Kurdistan Province</a> and nearby areas. In <a href="/wiki/Khuzestan" title="Khuzestan" class="mw-redirect">Khuzestan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Persian_dialects_in_Khuzestan" title="Persian dialects in Khuzestan">many distinct Persian dialects</a> are spoken. <a href="/wiki/Luri_language" title="Luri language">Luri</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lari_language" title="Lari language">Lari</a> languages are spoken in southwestern and southern Iran.</p> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Turkic_languages" title="Turkic languages">Turkic languages</a> and dialects, most importantly <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijani_language" title="Azerbaijani language">Azerbaijani language</a> which is by far the most spoken language in the country after Persian,<sup id="cite_ref-280" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-280">[279]</a></sup> are spoken in different areas in Iran, but is especially widely and dominantly spoken in <a href="/wiki/Iranian_Azerbaijan" title="Iranian Azerbaijan" class="mw-redirect">Iranian Azerbaijan</a>.</p> 
     <p>Notable minority languages in Iran include <a href="/wiki/Armenian_language" title="Armenian language">Armenian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Georgian_language" title="Georgian language">Georgian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Neo-Aramaic_languages" title="Neo-Aramaic languages">Neo-Aramaic</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Arabic" title="Arabic">Arabic</a>. <a href="/wiki/Khuzestani_Arabic" title="Khuzestani Arabic">Khuzi Arabic</a> is spoken by the <a href="/wiki/Ahwazi_Arabs" title="Ahwazi Arabs">Arabs in Khuzestan</a>, and the wider group of <a href="/wiki/Iranian_Arabs" title="Iranian Arabs">Iranian Arabs</a>. <a href="/wiki/Circassian_language" title="Circassian language">Circassian language</a> was also once widely used by the large Circassian minority, but, due to assimilation over the many years, no sizable number of Circassians speak the language anymore.<sup id="cite_ref-281" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-281">[280]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-282" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-282">[281]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-283" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-283">[282]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-284" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-284">[283]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Percentages of spoken language continue to be a point of debate, as many opt that they are politically motivated; most notably regarding the largest and second-largest ethnicities in Iran, the Persians and <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijanis" title="Azerbaijanis">Azerbaijanis</a>. The following percentages are according to the <a href="/wiki/CIA" title="CIA" class="mw-redirect">CIA</a>'s <a href="/wiki/World_Factbook" title="World Factbook" class="mw-redirect">World Factbook</a>: 53% Persian, 16% <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijani_language" title="Azerbaijani language">Azerbaijani</a>, 10% <a href="/wiki/Kurdish_language" title="Kurdish language" class="mw-redirect">Kurdish</a>, 7% <a href="/wiki/Mazandarani_language" title="Mazandarani language" class="mw-redirect">Mazenderani</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gilaki_language" title="Gilaki language">Gilaki</a>, 7% <a href="/wiki/Luri_language" title="Luri language">Luri</a>, 2% <a href="/wiki/Turkmen_language" title="Turkmen language">Turkmen</a>, 2% <a href="/wiki/Balochi_language" title="Balochi language">Balochi</a>, 2% <a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" title="Arabic language" class="mw-redirect">Arabic</a>, and 2% the remainder <a href="/wiki/Armenian_language" title="Armenian language">Armenian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Georgian_language" title="Georgian language">Georgian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Neo-Aramaic_language" title="Neo-Aramaic language" class="mw-redirect">Neo-Aramaic</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Circassian_language" title="Circassian language">Circassian</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_34-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-34">[34]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_groups">Ethnic groups</span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Ethnicities_in_Iran" title="Ethnicities in Iran">Ethnicities in Iran</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Iran_ethnoreligious_distribution_2004.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Iran_ethnoreligious_distribution_2004.jpg/220px-Iran_ethnoreligious_distribution_2004.jpg" width="220" height="218" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Iran_ethnoreligious_distribution_2004.jpg/330px-Iran_ethnoreligious_distribution_2004.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Iran_ethnoreligious_distribution_2004.jpg/440px-Iran_ethnoreligious_distribution_2004.jpg 2x" data-file-width="980" data-file-height="970"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Iran_ethnoreligious_distribution_2004.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> Iran's ethnoreligious distribution
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>As with the spoken languages, the ethnic group composition also remains a point of debate, mainly regarding the largest and second largest ethnic groups, the Persians and Azerbaijanis, due to the lack of Iranian state censuses based on ethnicity. <a href="/wiki/The_World_Factbook" title="The World Factbook">The CIA's World Factbook</a> has estimated that around 79% of the population of Iran are a diverse <a href="/wiki/Proto-Indo-Europeans" title="Proto-Indo-Europeans">Indo-European</a> <a href="/wiki/Ethnolinguistics" title="Ethnolinguistics">ethno-linguistic group</a> that comprise the speakers of <a href="/wiki/Iranian_languages" title="Iranian languages">Iranian languages</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-285" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-285">[284]</a></sup> with <a href="/wiki/Persian_people" title="Persian people">Persians</a> (incl. <a href="/wiki/Mazandarani_people" title="Mazandarani people" class="mw-redirect">Mazenderanis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gilaki_people" title="Gilaki people" class="mw-redirect">Gilaks</a>) constituting 61% of the population, <a href="/wiki/Kurds" title="Kurds">Kurds</a> 10%, <a href="/wiki/Lurs" title="Lurs">Lurs</a> 6%, and <a href="/wiki/Baloch_people" title="Baloch people">Balochs</a> 2%. Peoples of the other ethnicities in Iran make up the remaining 21%, with <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijani_people" title="Azerbaijani people" class="mw-redirect">Azerbaijanis</a> constituting 16%, <a href="/wiki/Arabs" title="Arabs">Arabs</a> 2%, <a href="/wiki/Turkmen_people" title="Turkmen people" class="mw-redirect">Turkmens</a> and <a href="/wiki/Turkic_peoples" title="Turkic peoples">Turkic tribes</a> 2%, and others 1% (such as <a href="/wiki/Armenians" title="Armenians">Armenians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Talysh_people" title="Talysh people">Talysh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Georgians" title="Georgians">Georgians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Circassians" title="Circassians">Circassians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Assyrians" title="Assyrians" class="mw-redirect">Assyrians</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_34-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-34">[34]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Library_of_Congress" title="Library of Congress">Library of Congress</a> issued slightly different estimates: Persians 65% (incl. Mazenderanis, Gilakis and Talysh), <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijani_people" title="Azerbaijani people" class="mw-redirect">Azerbaijanis</a> 16%, <a href="/wiki/Kurds" title="Kurds">Kurds</a> 7%, <a href="/wiki/Lurs" title="Lurs">Lurs</a> 6%, <a href="/wiki/Baloch_people" title="Baloch people">Baluchi</a> 2%; Turkic tribal groups such as <a href="/wiki/Qashqai_people" title="Qashqai people">Qashqai</a> 1%, and <a href="/wiki/Turkmens" title="Turkmens">Turkmens</a> 1%; and non-Iranian, non-Turkic groups such as <a href="/wiki/Armenians" title="Armenians">Armenians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Georgians" title="Georgians">Georgians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Assyrians" title="Assyrians" class="mw-redirect">Assyrians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Circassians" title="Circassians">Circassians</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Arabs" title="Arabs">Arabs</a> less than 3%. It determined that Persian is the first language of at least 65% of the country's population, and is the second language for most of the remaining 35%.<sup id="cite_ref-286" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-286">[285]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Other <a href="/wiki/Non-governmental" title="Non-governmental" class="mw-redirect">non-governmental</a> estimations regarding the groups other than the Persians and Azerbaijanis roughly congruate with the World Factbook and the Library of Congress. However, many scholarly and organisational estimations regarding the number of these two groups differ significantly from the mentioned census. According to many of them, the number of ethnic Azerbaijanis in Iran comprises between 21.6–30% of the total population, with the majority holding it on 25%.<sup class="reference plainlinks nourlexpansion" id="ref_New_America_Foundation"><a href="#endnote_New_America_Foundation">c</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-New_America_Foundation_287-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-New_America_Foundation-287">[286]</a></sup><sup class="reference plainlinks nourlexpansion" id="ref_Minority_Rights"><a href="#endnote_Minority_Rights">d</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Minority_Rights_288-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Minority_Rights-288">[287]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-289" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-289">[288]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-290" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-290">[289]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Criticism_291-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Criticism-291">[290]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-292" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-292">[291]</a></sup> In any case, the largest population of Azerbaijanis in the world live in Iran.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles: 
      <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Iran" title="Religion in Iran">Religion in Iran</a> and 
      <a href="/wiki/Irreligion_in_Iran" title="Irreligion in Iran">Irreligion in Iran</a>
     </div> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote">
      See also: 
      <a href="/wiki/Islamization_of_Iran" title="Islamization of Iran">Islamization of Iran</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px"> 
       <div style="background-color:white;margin:auto;position:relative;width:200px;height:200px;overflow:hidden"> 
        <p><br></p> 
        <p><br></p> 
        <p><br></p> 
        <p><br></p> 
        <p><br></p> 
        <p><br></p> 
        <div class="transborder" style="position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:0; top:0; border-width:0 200px 200px 0; border-color:SaddleBrown"></div> 
        <div class="transborder" style="position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:100px; top:100px; border-width:100px 0 0 3978.0357839777px; border-left-color:DodgerBlue"></div> 
        <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:DodgerBlue"></div> 
        <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 200px 0;border-color:DodgerBlue"></div> 
        <div class="transborder" style="position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:100px; top:100px; border-width:100px 0 0 2651.325628724px; border-left-color:MediumSeaGreen"></div> 
        <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:MediumSeaGreen"></div> 
        <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 200px 0;border-color:MediumSeaGreen"></div> 
        <div style="position:absolute;left:0;top:0">
         <img alt="Circle frame.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Circle_frame.svg/200px-Circle_frame.svg.png" width="200" height="200" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Circle_frame.svg/300px-Circle_frame.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Circle_frame.svg/400px-Circle_frame.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="200" data-file-height="200">
        </div> 
       </div> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <p>Religion in Iran (cen. 2011)<sup id="cite_ref-293" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-293">[292]</a></sup></p> 
        <div class="legend">
         <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:MediumSeaGreen; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;
         <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Iran" title="Islam in Iran">Islam</a>
         <sup id="cite_ref-294" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-294">[293]</a></sup> (99.4%)
        </div> 
        <div class="legend">
         <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:DodgerBlue; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;
         <a href="/wiki/Christianity_in_Iran" title="Christianity in Iran">Christianity</a>
         <sup id="cite_ref-295" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-295">[294]</a></sup> (0.2%)
        </div> 
        <div class="legend">
         <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:SaddleBrown; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;Other
         <sup id="cite_ref-296" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-296">[295]</a></sup> (0.6%)
        </div> 
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Historically, <a href="/wiki/Proto-Indo-Iranian_religion" title="Proto-Indo-Iranian religion">Proto-Iranian religion</a> and the subsequent <a href="/wiki/Zoroastrianism" title="Zoroastrianism">Zoroastrianism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Manichaeism" title="Manichaeism">Manichaeism</a> were the dominant religions in Iran, particularly during the <a href="/wiki/Medes" title="Medes">Median</a>, <a href="/wiki/Achaemenid_Empire" title="Achaemenid Empire">Achaemenid</a>, <a href="/wiki/Parthian_Empire" title="Parthian Empire">Parthian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sasanian_Empire" title="Sasanian Empire">Sassanid</a> empires. This changed after the fall of the Sassanid Empire by the <a href="/wiki/Muslim_conquest_of_Persia" title="Muslim conquest of Persia">Muslim Conquest of Iran</a>. Iran was predominantly <a href="/wiki/Sunni" title="Sunni" class="mw-redirect">Sunni</a> until <a href="/wiki/Safavid_conversion_of_Iran_to_Shia_Islam" title="Safavid conversion of Iran to Shia Islam">the conversion</a> of the country (as well as the people of what is today the neighboring <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Azerbaijan" title="Republic of Azerbaijan" class="mw-redirect">Republic of Azerbaijan</a>) to <a href="/wiki/Shia_Islam" title="Shia Islam">Shia Islam</a> by the order of the <a href="/wiki/Safavid_dynasty" title="Safavid dynasty">Safavid dynasty</a> in the 16th century.<sup id="cite_ref-Abdullah2014_107-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Abdullah2014-107">[106]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Today, the <a href="/wiki/Twelver" title="Twelver">Twelver</a> Shia Islam is the official <a href="/wiki/State_religion" title="State religion">state religion</a>, to which about 90% to 95%<sup id="cite_ref-297" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-297">[296]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-298" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-298">[297]</a></sup> of the population officially belong. About 4% to 8% of the population are <a href="/wiki/Sunni_Muslims" title="Sunni Muslims" class="mw-redirect">Sunni Muslims</a>, mainly <a href="/wiki/Iranian_Kurdistan" title="Iranian Kurdistan">Kurds</a> and <a href="/wiki/Baloch_people" title="Baloch people">Balochs</a>. The remaining 2% are non-Muslim <a href="/wiki/Religious_minorities_in_Iran" title="Religious minorities in Iran" class="mw-redirect">religious minorities</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Christians_in_Iran" title="Christians in Iran" class="mw-redirect">Christians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Persian_Jews" title="Persian Jews">Jews</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith" title="Bahá'í Faith">Bahais</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mandeans" title="Mandeans" class="mw-redirect">Mandeans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yezidi" title="Yezidi" class="mw-redirect">Yezidis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yarsan" title="Yarsan" class="mw-redirect">Yarsanis</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Zoroastrians_in_Iran" title="Zoroastrians in Iran">Zoroastrians</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_34-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-34">[34]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-saving_299-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-saving-299">[298]</a></sup></p> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Judaism" title="Judaism">Judaism</a> has a long history in Iran, dating back to the <a href="/wiki/Nabonidus#The_Persian_conquest_of_Babylonia" title="Nabonidus">Achaemenid Conquest of Babylonia</a>. Although many left in the wake of the establishment of the <a href="/wiki/State_of_Israel" title="State of Israel" class="mw-redirect">State of Israel</a> and the <a href="/wiki/1979_Revolution" title="1979 Revolution" class="mw-redirect">1979 Revolution</a>, around 8,756 Jews remain in Iran, according to the latest census.<sup id="cite_ref-IranCensusMurder_300-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IranCensusMurder-300">[299]</a></sup> Iran has the largest Jewish population in the Middle East outside of Israel.<sup id="cite_ref-301" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-301">[300]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Around 250,000–370,000 <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christians</a> reside in Iran,<sup id="cite_ref-Worldpopulationreview.com_November_29_2015c_302-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Worldpopulationreview.com_November_29_2015c-302">[301]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-303" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-303">[302]</a></sup> and it is the largest recognized minority religion in the nation. Most are of <a href="/wiki/Iranian_Armenians" title="Iranian Armenians">Armenian</a> background with a sizable minority of <a href="/wiki/Assyrians_in_Iran" title="Assyrians in Iran">Assyrians</a> as well.<sup id="cite_ref-IRFR2009-Iran_304-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IRFR2009-Iran-304">[303]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Christianity, Judaism, Zoroastrianism, and the Sunni branch of Islam are officially recognized by the government, and have reserved seats in the <a href="/wiki/Iranian_Parliament" title="Iranian Parliament" class="mw-redirect">Iranian Parliament</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Colin_Brock_p_99_127-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Colin_Brock_p_99-127">[126]</a></sup> But the <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith" title="Bahá'í Faith">Bahá'í Faith</a>, which is said to be the largest non-Muslim religious minority in Iran,<sup id="cite_ref-fdih2_305-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fdih2-305">[304]</a></sup> is not officially recognized, and has been persecuted during its existence in Iran since the 19th century. Since the 1979 Revolution, the <a href="/wiki/Persecution_of_Bahais" title="Persecution of Bahais" class="mw-redirect">persecution of Bahais</a> has increased with executions, the denial of civil rights and liberties, and the denial of access to higher education and employment.<sup id="cite_ref-fdih1_306-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fdih1-306">[305]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ihrdc_307-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ihrdc-307">[306]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-308" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-308">[307]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>The government has not released statistics regarding <a href="/wiki/Irreligion_in_Iran" title="Irreligion in Iran">irreligiosity</a>. However, the irreligious figures are growing and are higher in the <a href="/wiki/Iranian_diaspora" title="Iranian diaspora">diaspora</a>, notably among <a href="/wiki/Iranian_American#Religion" title="Iranian American" class="mw-redirect">Iranian Americans</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-309" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-309">[308]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-irreligion_310-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-irreligion-310">[309]</a></sup></p>

     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Iran" title="Culture of Iran">Culture of Iran</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The earliest recorded cultures within the region of Iran date back to the <a href="/wiki/Lower_Paleolithic" title="Lower Paleolithic">Lower Paleolithic</a> era.</p> 
     <p>Owing to its dominant geopolitical position and culture in the world, Iran has directly influenced cultures as far away as <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a>, <a href="/wiki/Macedonia_(region)" title="Macedonia (region)">Macedonia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a> to the West, <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a> to the North, the <a href="/wiki/Arabian_Peninsula" title="Arabian Peninsula">Arabian Peninsula</a> to the South, and indirectly <a href="/wiki/South_Asia" title="South Asia">South</a> and <a href="/wiki/East_Asia" title="East Asia">East Asia</a> to the East.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Art">Art</span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles: 
      <a href="/wiki/Iranian_art" title="Iranian art" class="mw-redirect">Iranian art</a> and 
      <a href="/wiki/Persian_carpet" title="Persian carpet">Persian carpet</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Isfahan_Lotfollah_mosque_ceiling_symmetric.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Isfahan_Lotfollah_mosque_ceiling_symmetric.jpg/220px-Isfahan_Lotfollah_mosque_ceiling_symmetric.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Isfahan_Lotfollah_mosque_ceiling_symmetric.jpg/330px-Isfahan_Lotfollah_mosque_ceiling_symmetric.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Isfahan_Lotfollah_mosque_ceiling_symmetric.jpg/440px-Isfahan_Lotfollah_mosque_ceiling_symmetric.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2981" data-file-height="1996"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Isfahan_Lotfollah_mosque_ceiling_symmetric.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> Ceiling of the 
        <a href="/wiki/Lotfollah_Mosque" title="Lotfollah Mosque" class="mw-redirect">Lotfollah Mosque</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Miniator_hotel_shah_abbas_deevar.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Miniator_hotel_shah_abbas_deevar.jpg/220px-Miniator_hotel_shah_abbas_deevar.jpg" width="220" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Miniator_hotel_shah_abbas_deevar.jpg/330px-Miniator_hotel_shah_abbas_deevar.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Miniator_hotel_shah_abbas_deevar.jpg/440px-Miniator_hotel_shah_abbas_deevar.jpg 2x" data-file-width="756" data-file-height="525"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Miniator_hotel_shah_abbas_deevar.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Safavid_art" title="Safavid art">Safavid painting</a> kept at the 
        <a href="/wiki/Abbasi_Hotel" title="Abbasi Hotel">Abbasi Caravanserai</a> in 
        <a href="/wiki/Isfahan" title="Isfahan">Isfahan</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Iranian works of art show a great variety in style, in different regions and periods. The main connections between these works are <a href="/wiki/Iconographic" title="Iconographic" class="mw-redirect">iconographic</a> motifs.<sup id="cite_ref-311" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-311">[310]</a></sup> Combination is another major element in the art of Iran, specifically the depictions of composite human and animal figures, which also refer to the <a href="/wiki/Iranian_mythology" title="Iranian mythology">mythology of Iran</a>.</p> 
     <p>Iranian art encompasses many disciplines, including <a href="/wiki/Architecture" title="Architecture">architecture</a>, <a href="/wiki/Painting" title="Painting">painting</a>, <a href="/wiki/Weaving" title="Weaving">weaving</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pottery" title="Pottery">pottery</a>, <a href="/wiki/Calligraphy" title="Calligraphy">calligraphy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Metalworking" title="Metalworking">metalworking</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Stonemasonry" title="Stonemasonry">stonemasonry</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Median_Empire" title="Median Empire" class="mw-redirect">Median</a> and <a href="/wiki/Achaemenid" title="Achaemenid" class="mw-redirect">Achaemenid</a> empires left a significant classical art scene which remained as basic influences for the art of the later eras. Art of the Parthians was a mixture of Iranian and <a href="/wiki/Hellenistic_art" title="Hellenistic art">Hellenistic</a> artworks, with their main motifs being scenes of royal hunting expeditions and <a href="/wiki/Investiture" title="Investiture">investitures</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-312" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-312">[311]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-313" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-313">[312]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Sassanid_art" title="Sassanid art" class="mw-redirect">Sassanid art</a> played a prominent role in the formation of both European and Asian <a href="/wiki/Medieval_art" title="Medieval art">medieval art</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Iransaga:_The_art_of_Sassanians_82-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Iransaga:_The_art_of_Sassanians-82">[81]</a></sup> which carried forward to the <a href="/wiki/Islamic_world" title="Islamic world" class="mw-redirect">Islamic world</a>, and much of what later became known as Islamic learning, such as <a href="/wiki/Philology" title="Philology">philology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Islamic_literature" title="Islamic literature">literature</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fiqh" title="Fiqh">jurisprudence</a>, <a href="/wiki/Early_Islamic_philosophy" title="Early Islamic philosophy">philosophy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Islamic_medicine" title="Islamic medicine" class="mw-redirect">medicine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Islamic_architecture" title="Islamic architecture">architecture</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Islamic_science" title="Islamic science" class="mw-redirect">science</a>, were of Sassanid basis.<sup id="cite_ref-314" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-314">[313]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-315" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-315">[314]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Iran_in_Britannica_316-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Iran_in_Britannica-316">[315]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>There is also a vibrant <a href="/wiki/Iranian_modern_and_contemporary_art" title="Iranian modern and contemporary art">Iranian modern and contemporary art</a> scene, with its genesis in the late 1940s. The 1949 <i>Apadana Gallery</i> of <a href="/wiki/Tehran" title="Tehran">Tehran</a>, which was operated by Mahmoud Javadi Pour and other colleagues, and the emergence of artists such as <a href="/wiki/Marcos_Grigorian" title="Marcos Grigorian">Marcos Grigorian</a> in the 1950s, signaled a commitment to the creation of a form of modern art grounded in Iran.<sup id="cite_ref-317" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-317">[316]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Iranian <a href="/wiki/Carpet" title="Carpet">carpet</a>-<a href="/wiki/Weaving" title="Weaving">weaving</a> dates back to the <a href="/wiki/Bronze_Age" title="Bronze Age">Bronze Age</a>, and is one of the most distinguished manifestations of the art of Iran. Iran is the world's largest producer and exporter of handmade carpets, producing three quarters of the world's total output and having a share of 30% of world's export markets.<sup id="cite_ref-Goswami2009_318-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Goswami2009-318">[317]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-319" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-319">[318]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Iran is also home to one of the <a href="/wiki/Iranian_Crown_Jewels" title="Iranian Crown Jewels">largest jewel collections</a> in the world.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Architecture">Architecture</span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles: 
      <a href="/wiki/Iranian_architecture" title="Iranian architecture">Iranian architecture</a> and 
      <a href="/wiki/Persian_gardens" title="Persian gardens">Persian gardens</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The history of Iranian architecture goes back to the <a href="/wiki/7th_millennium_BC" title="7th millennium BC">7th millennium BC</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-320" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-320">[319]</a></sup> Iranians were among the first to use <a href="/wiki/Mathematics" title="Mathematics">mathematics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Geometry" title="Geometry">geometry</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Astronomy" title="Astronomy">astronomy</a> in architecture.</p> 
     <p>Iranian architecture displays great variety, both structural and aesthetic, developing gradually and coherently out of earlier traditions and experience.<sup id="cite_ref-321" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-321">[320]</a></sup> The guiding motifs of Iranian architecture are unity, continuity, and cosmic <a href="/wiki/Symbol" title="Symbol">symbolism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-322" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-322">[321]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Iran ranks seventh among countries with the most archaeological architectural ruins and attractions from antiquity, as recognized by <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-323" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-323">[322]</a></sup></p> 
     <div style="clear:both;"></div>
